Free Talk

A Laughing Matter 92

— Hai Ke

A—Your house is the best. Is it your own or are you renting it?

B—I am renting it, but it's as good as my own.

A—Why?

B—Because I haven't paid the rent for six or seven months.

A—Oh? Why is your face so pale? You look terrible. Are you sick?

B—I'm not sick.

A—Then what's bothering you?

B—Just now someone tried to sell me an old car. He said that even though the car is very old, I can use it for as long as I live. When I looked at the car, I couldn't help but worry about how long I have left to live.

Mother—I gave you that apple. Why aren't you eating it?

Young daughter—I'm waiting for my brother to come back from school.

Mother—Do you want to share half with him?

Young daughter—No. When I eat something, it tastes better if someone is watching.

A—I had the most embarrassing thing happen to me today.

B—What happened?

A—My neighbor, Mr. Wang, had guests over and borrowed all my dishes and cups. But he didn't invite me.

Japan's Sexist Practices 93

— Yan Ye

Today, the islands of Japan have become one of the world's civilized countries. However, the sexist practices in its society are even worse than in our country. Recently, a friend who has lived in Japan for a long time returned and told me many stories of gender inequality in Japan. I will record a few of them to tell the readers.

In Japanese elementary schools, there are always more male teachers than female teachers. In Tokyo, for example, male graduates of teacher training colleges in their first year of service earn 55 yuan a month, while women only earn 45 yuan. With the same qualifications and the same ability, and the duties are the same, and the effort is the same, the unequal treatment is so great. The sexism is obvious. As for the subsidies received by teacher training students while studying at school, women also receive less than men. Women only receive 12 yuan and 90 cents per month, while men receive 13 yuan and 50 cents.

The education sector, which should have high levels of knowledge, looks down on women as described above. Then it is easy to imagine other fields. Company employees and shop assistants have much lower pay than men. Men always say that women are incompetent and only worthy of being raised. Women also see themselves as weak and do not dare to resist. My friend's daughter graduated from university last summer. She heard that a certain organization had a secretarial position open, with a monthly salary of 80 yuan. After much effort, she finally got the job. On the day she took office, the head of the organization told her all the precautions for her duties. When he mentioned her monthly salary, it was only 60 yuan. The woman said, "Why is it suddenly reduced by 20 yuan?" The head said, "The figure of 80 yuan is for men. Do you, a weak woman, also want to compete with men for equality?" The woman was extremely angry when she heard this. She resigned and went home. When she got home, she went to her bedroom and sobbed. Her parents quickly asked her what was wrong. The woman sobbed and told them. The father said, "Sexism has been around since ancient times. How can you not know your limits and try to compete with others?" The woman became even more angry and felt so hopeless that she tried to end her life with three feet of white silk that evening. Fortunately, she was discovered and a tragedy was averted. As of now, my friend has returned to his home country, and the woman is still living at home, unwilling to set foot in society.

Sexism is even more severe in rural Japan. In a family, the husband is like the emperor of heaven, and the wife is like a servant. When the husband returns from outside, the wife must greet him with a smile, relieve him of his burden, and offer him tea and cigarettes, as if welcoming a distinguished guest. The husband receives it with arrogance and does not say a word of thanks. When he returns in the evening, the wife must also prepare his favorite foods. The husband eats and the wife serves him. She responds to his every call. Even an extremely poor husband, who works as a hired laborer during the day, treats his wife like an animal in the evening, and her status is very high.

My Opinion on Suicide Prevention 94

— Xie Lu

In recent years, the number of young people committing suicide has been increasing every day. Even if it is caused by environmental pressure, it is still a shame that young people do not know how to fight. The life solutions mentioned in Free Talk by Tian Xuwo Sheng and another gentleman are very well-intentioned. After all, the difficulties of life are the main cause of suicide. It must be known that in this world, customs are decadent, the cost of living is high, and it is difficult to find work. The strong become bandits, and the weak become pessimistic and degenerate. Both tend towards suicide. Some have weak wills and are degenerate and romantic, and end up taking their own lives. Others have been unemployed for a long time, their families are heavily burdened, they have no one to turn to, and they cannot borrow money, so they resort to suicide. Still others are disappointed in love or fail in school, become immersed in degenerate literature, and are fascinated by biased and heretical ideas. All of these are secondary causes of suicide. Once the causes are identified, the remedies can be clarified. The increasing level of social and economic progress is a trend of the world and cannot be avoided. If society is extravagant and indulgent, this is a gradual trend of evil. If one can strengthen one's will, there is no need to be affected. For example, if one always reads erotic novels and then suddenly reads the works of the Qin and Han dynasties, one will find the erotic novels shallow and unreadable. Therefore, people only seek the new, and I only seek the old. There is great pleasure in this. No matter how evil the social trends are, one will not be affected at all. As for the difficulties of life, one should work hard to increase income and be frugal to reduce expenses, study to find employment, and be honest to establish oneself. No matter how urgent the world changes, one should not change my words. Why should one resort to suicide? Lao Tzu said, "I have a great worry, which is that I have a body. If I had no body, what would I have to worry about?" Mountain Valley Elder said, "The bodies of all living beings are the same as the void. Where can worries find a place to rest?" If one's body is the same as the void and one regards one's body as nothing, then worries and gains and losses cannot enter. Love and money are even more irrelevant to my body. The true meaning of life is that, in the big picture, it benefits the country, and in the small picture, it benefits society. The highest is to establish virtue, the next is to establish merit, and the next is to establish words. One should maintain a spirit of struggle and an optimistic attitude. The world's eccentric Napoleon said, "The word 'difficult' exists only in the dictionary of fools." Conan Doyle said, "Life moves forward only. Why look back?" These are all things that young people should take as their guiding principles. Alas, today is a chaotic world. I do not want young people to learn from Lord Xinling's wine and women, nor do I want them to learn from the Jin people's crazy behavior. If there is no other way, they should learn from Yuanming and Yaofu. In addition, the prohibition of degenerate novels, the promotion of birth control, and the dissemination of correct views on life are all important strategies for saving the situation that those who care about the world should pay attention to. Alas, suicide is the act of a coward. Good young people, hurry up and work hard!

Random Notes 95

— Xu Bi Bo

The Wu Men Xing She [Poetry Society] was established on the Qixi Festival [Double Seventh Festival] of this year, marking its tenth anniversary. In recent years, members have been running around in all directions due to livelihood issues. Those remaining in Suzhou do not even account for four-tenths. Therefore, the monthly gatherings that were once customary have faded away. Only the Qixi Festival, as the anniversary of its establishment, sees a gathering without fail. This year marks the tenth anniversary, so we should add some embellishments to commemorate it. However, fellow members are preoccupied with worldly affairs. Those from distant places have not yet prepared to return, and even the ten or so members residing in Shanghai have not arrived. It's truly disappointing.

The banquet that evening was held at Mingdao Mansion. Mingdao has a bad leg. His old illness recurred in early summer, causing him great pain. Even after being treated by dozens of Chinese and Western doctors, he has not improved. He sits all day, living in solitude and without joy. The doctors also warned him not to overthink, but the requests for manuscripts from various bookstores and newspapers piled up, which he couldn't fulfill. Yanhqiao temporarily took over his teaching position at Zhenhua School. Moreover, due to business reasons, his friend at Youlian urged him to quickly finish drafting volumes five and six of "The Female Knight-Errant of Desolate Rivers". I couldn't bear to see him in that state, but as I was under orders, I had to relay the message. He politely replied that he would prioritize that when he had time. He was rather somber when he said that. Yanhqiao, due to his aversion to heat, spends his days in a bamboo forest from summer to autumn. He says that when he's deeply absorbed, he's not only oblivious to the heat, but he also loses track of time and place. He's truly in a state of abandon. This man's luck is shining brightly; every time he plays mahjong, he wins. [A metaphor where "South" represents winning]. This is in stark contrast to my recent streak of losses.

Xiao Qing has recently developed a fondness for traditional Chinese painting. She's learning flower painting from the renowned painter Chen Huian, and she's quickly gaining recognition for surpassing her teacher. This past month, she painted four silk fan pages, each seven inches square. One of them was purchased by an Englishman named Small for sixteen shillings, which was equivalent to thirteen yuan, eight jiao, and four fen in Chinese silver dollars at the time. Perhaps "Small" is a case of mutual affection from a young age? The other three were purchased by an American woman, Miss Henry, for ten US dollars each, which was equivalent to thirty-five Chinese silver dollars. As a newly emerging painter, she's already selling to foreigners. Her future is bright, and her income will surely be much greater than that of writing detective novels.

Mianyun is a collector of fans. He has amassed no less than five hundred fan leaves and faces. Many of them are exquisite. Recently, he planned to commission a fan painting from a famous artist, willing to spend thirty dollars. However, he's worried that the artist is too temperamental and might not deliver the painting for years. Yanhqiao is well-acquainted with the painter, so he promised to urge the artist. Mianyun was overjoyed.

Zhanlu is calm and indifferent by nature, and he avoids conflict. Readers are constantly urging him to continue writing his "Lake and Sea Heroes". He only responds with a subtle smile. Peiyu has resigned from his position at the Shanghai school and taken a job as an editor at the World Book Company in Suzhou. That day, Sun Ji from Jun held a fan page and asked members of Xing Lü [Star Companion magazine] to sign it on behalf of a friend. Initially, I assumed there would be many signatures, but only eight members attended the gathering. So, his friend only received eight signatures.

Among the members in Suzhou who were absent, I heard that Yinqiu declined due to illness. Junbo has been preoccupied with the problem of the "Mysterious View Temple Wall", worrying about raising funds day and night. He had no time to attend. Jihe is lost in the bamboo forest. As for the absence of Elder Fengyin, I don't know why.

The Internal Politics of Post-War Poland (1) 96

— Li Liu Zeng, sent from Paris

It has been a decade since Poland was restored. From the surface, it appears that the more than twenty-eight million people of the country are united under the banner of the republic. The nation seems to be completely unified. However, upon closer examination, we find that internal politics are not entirely consistent. To illustrate with a minor example, the procedures for Poles to obtain identity cards vary depending on their place of birth. Some require a birth certificate issued by the mayor, while others require a baptismal certificate from a priest. The situation in the East and West is vastly different.

However, if we consider that Poland's true independence only began in 1918, then this diversity is not surprising. Poland was divided for 124 years, under the domination of the three great powers of Russia, Germany, and Austria. Its inherent culture was almost completely destroyed. As a result of the partition, both spiritually and materially, it changed gradually in three different environments, causing Poland to form three different regions, losing the commonalities of a single ancestral country. At the beginning of the Great War, the governments of Germany and Austria jointly ordered Marshal Pilsudski to form the Polish Legions to assist Germany and Austria. Meanwhile, countless Polish soldiers joined the Russian army to fight, under the command of Grand Duke Nicholas. Nicholas also promised Polish autonomy. After the retreat of the Russian army, the German army occupied the entire territory of Poland, giving Poland the appearance of unity. In 1916, in order to get Poland to join the war, the Germans even allowed the Poles to celebrate their national day and recognized Polish independence. However, this independence was nominal only until the end of the Great War. Poland gained true freedom from the day of the armistice. Before that, Poles joined the Allied Powers to attack the Central Powers, or joined the Allied Powers to attack the Allies in order to fight for the independence of their homeland. They killed each other, subject to the whims of fate. Only at this time did they achieve their common goal: to unite and complete Poland's independence.

At this time, everything in Poland's internal politics was in its infancy. The Polish People's Militia was the beginning of the Polish army. The Warsaw City Guard was the beginning of the Polish police. The Council of Regency, established in 1917, was the beginning of the Polish government. (This Council of Regency transferred power to Marshal Pilsudski on November 14, 1918.) At this time, the organization of the new Poland was nothing more than this. Internally, it had to fight against famine, bandits, and various disasters caused by war and subjugation. Externally, the national borders were not yet defined, and it had to defend against the encroachment of strong neighbors. The weight of its responsibilities far exceeded its capabilities.

European Travel Notes (73) 97

— Liu Haisu

A Visit to the Palace of Versailles (7) Versailles

The modern European art scene has a generation of Diabolism painters. They also seek to depict all the dark aspects, expressing the excitement of evil. There's nothing strange about this. They are simply trying to thoroughly understand human nature, just like gourmets who love to eat unusual flavors—like Chinese people's love of stinky fermented bean curd, preserved eggs, and spicy pickled vegetables; Japanese people's love of takuan pickles; and Westerners' love of cheese. If someone cannot appreciate that peculiar taste, they cannot discuss China, Japan, or the West. I kept talking to Mr. Chen all the way, running from the Versailles palace gardens outwards. When we walked out of the grand square behind the palace, the clouds in the sky were scattered by the wind. A long rainbow rose from the rooftops on the left and fell into the groves on the right, forming a 180-degree arc. Its brilliant and ever-changing colors astonished and bewildered us. Ah, this is our glory, that fleeting glory!

After visiting the Palace of Versailles, I often think that such a vast and magnificent garden, such a splendid and solemn palace, could only be created by a monarch with genius and a hedonistic nature. It could only be done under the autocratic rule of a monarch who believed, "I am the state." Indeed, during the reigns of Louis XIV and Louis XV, the French monarchy had reached its peak, and the power of autocracy was at its zenith. The extravagance of court life at that time is also enough to amaze us.

The palace alone employed 4,000 people, with 9,005 Swiss guards protecting the gates—the guards of the French court at that time were all Swiss, due to their unwavering loyalty. The royal family comprised more than 2,000 people, totaling 16,000. The annual expenditure was 20 million. The palace maids' food and drink cost 8 million a year. If we include occasional rewards and embezzled funds, palace officials received salaries of hundreds but actually obtained thousands. The palace maids were numerous and had no duties, spending their days on adornment. The royal kitchen cost 1.46 million each year and employed 295 chefs. The head chef earned 34,000 a year, and the wine expenses alone amounted to 4 million. Fish and bird expenses were 400,000. The palace had 4,000 horses, 220 carriages, and 1,500 strong men in the royal guard, costing 3 million. Actors, grooms, and hunting dogs all lived near the palace. The hunting grounds, strictly forbidden to the public, surrounded the palace for 120 *li*. The king and nobles hunted rabbits, pigs, deer, and countless other animals at will, spending 480,000 a year. From 1755 to 1769, in the span of 14 years, there were 144 boar hunts, 131 deer hunts, 266 rabbit and sheep hunts, and 25 fowl hunts, each lasting five or three days. There were also twelve detached palaces, costing over 1 million a year, with repair expenses of over 800,000. Whenever the king went hunting or on excursions, from nobles and palace attendants to servants and grooms, everyone followed. The daily expenses for accompanying people alone amounted to 100,000. In 14 years, besides hunting, the king made 234 tours. The king's private income was 200 million a year, and a ring for the queen was worth 3 million. Close attendants received annual salaries of 13 million. Such extravagance! Flipping through the pages of our own imperial history, only Emperor Yang of the Sui Dynasty and Emperor Ming of the Tang Dynasty can be compared to this.

Louis XIV was indeed a monarch of genius. He not only indulged in personal pleasure but also seized power through pleasure. He worked daily to weaken the feudal lords and suppress the nobility, turning feudal holdings into mere honorary titles. He lavishly decorated the palaces and indulged in hunting, entertainment, and sensual pleasures, thereby gathering the feudal lords at the palace, holding endless nights of revelry, valuing idle talk, and disdaining official duties. He subtly eroded their ambition to resist orders based on their territories, effectively destroying hundreds of thousands of feudal states in one fell swoop, achieving the unification of his royal power, and ushering in the glorious era of the French monarchy. However, while the hidden dangers of feudalism were eliminated, the suffering of the people was not alleviated. At that time, the nobles regarded the people as mere grass, trampling on them without the slightest compassion, extracting their wealth and sucking their blood. The oppression of autocracy had reached its extreme. However, the pressure of autocracy could only destroy the thoughts of ordinary people but could not stop the resistance of thinkers. Therefore, a group of great thinkers emerged in France at that time, serving as the driving force to resist this autocratic government, ultimately leading to the French Revolution.

Commercial News and Finance: Last Week's Soaring Market

Gold Market Fluctuates Unsteadily Throughout the Week: Last week, the gold market rebounded, presenting a soaring trend, albeit with occasional ups and downs. Hovering around 560 *taels*, with daily fluctuations of six to seven *taels*, the bewildered state of affairs seemed unstoppable. This was mainly due to the large-scale sale of silver bars by Citibank and India, which stimulated speculators to take advantage of the activity. However, rumors spread, and overseas telegrams were contradictory, causing confusion in the industry, with both buying and selling creating a complex situation. Starting from the beginning of the week, the market turned upward, surpassing the 60 *tael* mark. The subsequent rise and fall were unpredictable, and the market briefly entered a state of decline. Towards the weekend, the market recovered, showing excellent momentum. On September 3 (Wednesday), the price reached 567.8 *taels*, but on September 5 (Friday), it suddenly plummeted to 552.4 *taels*. This week saw a total fluctuation of 15.4 *taels*. However, large silver bars unexpectedly lengthened by 3.125, and the advance bill was extended by one and a half marks, which was contrary to the auction price, indicating a divergent trend. In short, the gold market remained unstable, but those with long positions in the industry fared better. As for the daily gold auction price, the initial decrease was slightly over 60 *taels*, but ultimately only decreased by less than 50 *taels*. The spot market has seen mediocre sales recently, with prices approximately 22 to 23 *taels* higher than the term auction. All September receipts that have not yet been rolled over were settled with public orders (cash) starting from the first of this month. It is said that the amount was enormous, approximately 20,000 *taels*. The daily progress of the past week is described in detail below.

Full Week Results in a Gain of 10.02 *Taels*: Since September 1 (the beginning of the week), British silver continued to rise, American silver remained unchanged, and advance bills remained steady, but internal conditions tightened, resulting in a rebound after repeated declines in the gold market. The opening price for October was an immediate increase to 555.3 *taels*. Subsequently, buying activity picked up, gradually rising by over 4 *taels*. Yuan Cheng, Yong Zuo, Tai Tai, Kang Run, and others all made purchases. In the afternoon, the price broke through the 60 *tael* mark, closing at 59.5 *taels*. The next day, large bars fell back, advance bills remained unchanged, and the internal market fluctuated slightly, ultimately appearing weak. The auction price softened slightly, with the front market briefly falling to slightly over 55 *taels*, but the rise and fall only amounted to 3.3 or 3.4 *taels*. Afterwards, the market suddenly turned upward, breaking through the 60 *tael* mark, due to rumors circulating in the market that the United States and India were selling large quantities of silver bars. Consequently, major players such as Fu Chang, Cui Da, Tai Da, and Decheng scrambled to buy. The price then retreated by 2 *taels* due to selling by Xin Heng and others. Wednesday saw a sudden surge, with major players pursuing purchases. Although silver bars lengthened, the price of silver remained unchanged, and the foreign exchange market was stable. The price abruptly broke out of the 60 *tael* range. In the afternoon, the market showed even greater momentum due to the shrinking of Indian remittances and rumors of continued silver sales from India, which boosted confidence and caused the price to soar to 67.8 *taels*. Subsequently, the price sharply decreased by 2 *taels*, resulting in a total fluctuation of over 10 *taels* that day. The following day, large bars fell back, but advance bills loosened, putting pressure on the gold market. This was due to a Reuters report stating that India denied selling silver bars, causing confidence to rapidly soften and the price to fall by 7 *taels*, breaking below the 60 *tael* mark. On Friday, large bars lengthened again, the foreign exchange market, which had been unchanged for many days, suddenly increased by one and a half marks. Furthermore, due to a Reuters report stating that the United States had not sold silver but had instead made purchases, industry sentiment was dampened. Zhi Feng, Yong Bing, Xing, and others successively sold, causing the price to fall to 52.4 *taels* in the morning. The momentum of long positions subsequently weakened, and the market softened slightly in the afternoon. On Saturday, the silver market increased slightly and was not shaken. Furthermore, the European market appeared soft, especially the United States, which seemed to have slightly sold silver. Consequently, the Shanghai foreign exchange market trended higher, and the price of gold once again exceeded the 60 *tael* mark, reaching 64 *taels*. Yuan Mao, Yong Yuan Cheng, Yong Fu Chang, and goods companies all made purchases, and no one dared to take short positions. Ultimately, the price was calculated at 62.7 *taels*, an increase of 10.02 *taels* compared to the previous Saturday, August 30. There is no concern about a potential decline in the future due to the approaching rollover date. The high and low prices of British, American, and Indian silver markets, as well as advance bills and auction prices, are listed below.

Yesterday was Sunday. According to telegrams from London, large silver bars saw a reduction of 1/875, to 16 5/8 pence (equivalent to 1 shilling 7 5/8 pence). Telegrams from New York indicated that American silver prices had risen 3/875, with spot prices at 35/8. Bank Closure Day, Silver Call Slightly Brisk 99

Yesterday was Sunday, and banks were closed as usual. Trading in the money market was also relatively quiet. The price for making *li* was 7 *qian* 2 *fen* 8 *li* 7 *hao* and a half in the morning market and 7 *qian* 2 *fen* 8 *li* 8 *hao* and seven-eighths in the afternoon market. The results were the same as the previous day. The transaction volume for interbank transfers was 395,000 in the morning market and 235,000 in the afternoon market. There were no transactions in banknotes in either the morning or afternoon markets. Over-the-counter banknotes traded 94,000 *zi* in the morning market and 42,000 in the afternoon market. Silver call for both morning and afternoon markets was uniformly 3 *fen*, slightly more brisk compared to the previous days. There were no reports of silver dollar transactions or collections from banks. Money shops collected over 3.2 million in silver dollar public orders and over 21 million in silver public orders. Remittances from various sources amounted to over 500,000. Small money shops traded over 400,000 in banknotes and remittances. In the auxiliary coin market, Jiangnan small dollars were 6 *qian* 4 *fen* 6 *li* in the morning market and 6 *qian* 4 *fen* 7 *li* in the afternoon market, the same as the previous day. The transaction volume was 1,000 *jiao* in the morning market and 3,500 *jiao* in the afternoon market. Incoming currencies from Hangzhou amounted to 240,000 in new currency. Incoming currency and banknotes from the Yangtze River area amounted to over 200,000, totaling over 300,000.

Securities: Bond Prices Increase Sharply Last Week 100

Turnover of 67.7 Million Yuan

Last week, the local securities market saw quiet spot trading in various public bonds, with a total turnover of only 83,500 yuan. This included 26,300 yuan in Disbandment bonds, 25,000 yuan in Troop Reduction bonds, 17,000 yuan in Customs bonds, and only 6-7,000 yuan each in Reorganization and Post-War bonds. Continued Finance bonds saw only 1,000 yuan traded, and other bonds saw no transactions. Futures trading was more active than the previous week, and the market atmosphere was lively. Both Troop Reduction and Disbandment bonds saw large-scale trading daily. Customs bonds were also more active than the previous week, while Post-War bonds were quiet. Other bonds remained scarce. Currently, market trading has gradually concentrated on the three bonds of Troop Reduction, Disbandment, and Customs, while others have lost their former position in the market. Daily transactions reached 13 million on Monday and Thursday-Friday and over 10 million on Wednesday. Tuesday and Saturday were quieter, with approximately 9 million yuan each. The total turnover was 67,748,500 yuan, an increase of over 15 million compared to the previous week. This included 11,910,000 for September Disbandment bonds, 10,490,000 for October Disbandment bonds, 10,245,000 for September Troop Reduction bonds, 15,245,000 for October Troop Reduction bonds, 6,775,000 for September Customs bonds, 5,960,000 for October Customs bonds, 1,555,000 for September Post-War bonds, 1,835,000 for October Post-War bonds, 585,000 for September Reorganization bonds, 330,000 for October Reorganization bonds, 435,000 for September 96 bonds, and 520,000 for October 96 bonds. There were no transactions in Continued 25 or Continued Rolling bonds in October, with approximately 280,000 yuan each traded for September. Finance bonds traded 10,000 yuan, and 1,035,000 yuan was traded in 19-year Cigarette bonds. As for the price fluctuations of each bond, although the overall trend was stable throughout the week, with no major rises or falls daily, the good military news from the front and the optimistic situation led to positive market sentiment and active investment purchases. Consequently, buyers consistently dominated, and bond prices steadily trended upward. Except for slight weakness on the weekend and Monday, prices rose on all other days. As a result, compared to the previous week, only Reorganization, Finance, and 96 Continued Rolling bonds saw minimal changes, while Troop Reduction bonds soared by 4 yuan, Customs and Continued 25 bonds increased by over 3 yuan, and Disbandment and Post-War bonds also increased by several yuan. The upward trend was quite strong. Observing the bond market situation, if the environment does not change, a slight stabilization can be expected. Yarn and Cotton: Yarn Market Increases Slightly Last Week 101

Spot Sales Extremely Quiet... Inventory Increases

The yarn market showed a rather sluggish trend at the beginning of the week. The domestic war continued, sales were obstructed, and the purchasing power of all parties was weak, resulting in a gradual increase in the inventory of yarn in Shanghai. According to a survey by Japanese merchants, there were approximately 130,000 to 140,000 bales. With such a huge amount, it was increasingly difficult for the market to recover. Moreover, a large portion of the inventory was unsalable. There had been no procurement from the Yangtze River area for a long time, and rampant banditry and military changes in the north made the outlook for yarn sales extremely pessimistic. In South China, most of the goods shipped by the Guangdong merchants the other day were still at their destination, making the current demand particularly quiet. In addition, the overseas cotton yarn market was still in decline, putting even greater pressure on the market. The Guangdong merchants, who had been most enthusiastic the other day, had been vigorously searching for futures in the market and absorbing large quantities. However, given the poor environment and sluggish spot sales, the general trend was to release the purchased volume. Consequently, the market trended downwards. However, a certain manufacturer with a long position remained unmoved. The Japanese merchants and some others needed to see 50 *taels* for customs clearance. According to statistics, the total volume purchased by various guilds that day was 6,285 bales, with 2,035 bales purchased by fellow merchants. The prices for Japanese yarn fell by 1-2 *taels*. Auction participants initially released long positions, causing market prices to fall. Later, Ruida made up for 6-7,000 bales, and the market slightly rebounded. As a result, the prices for all months fell to a low point of 1-2.3 *qian* compared to the previous week, with distant months reaching 151.1 *taels*. The total turnover for the week was 74,600 bales. Although Osaka's three-item production has been reduced significantly, the upward momentum remains lacking, and the overall trend is volatile. Cotton Market Remains Weak Last Week 102

The overall situation of the cotton market remained weak and sluggish. Since the overseas cotton market still could not be optimistic, sellers were extremely active at the beginning of the week. In previous years, before the new cotton entered the market, Japanese merchants would have purchased large quantities of distant-month new cotton for storage. However, this year, because there was a surplus of raw materials worldwide and Indian cotton prices were extremely cheap, various factories had absorbed as much as possible. It was said that they had enough to meet their needs for five or six months, and this factory also had such a large amount in storage. Moreover, the price of new cotton was high, so there was naturally no need to purchase it. Therefore, the quietness of the new cotton trade was rare in history. Consequently, most manufacturers viewed the market as bearish. Shortly thereafter, the weather turned unfavorable, with alternating periods of cloudiness and sunshine. As a result, buyers seized the opportunity to purchase and increase their holdings. General cotton merchants debated extensively, and for a time, there was a strong upward trend. However, the global situation remained pessimistic, and new buyers were still lacking. The market fell again. The rainy weather for several days naturally caused damage, but fortunately, the rain did not last long, and there was no wind. It was said that the damage in Hubei was still light. The market suddenly strengthened at the weekend because American cotton weekly reports had a bullish tone, predicting a decrease in the second production estimate. Ruida, a major player, had a significant amount of short-covering, tightening the market. The price rose by four or five *qian* in one day. American cotton prices had reached the lowest level in ten years. However, consumption could not be stimulated in a short period, and the future remained uncertain. The outlook for local cotton was extremely bullish, but the demand from various factories remained unchanged. In addition, the yarn market was weak. The Han Standard prices on the exchange increased by three or four *qian* for each month compared to the previous week due to the unfavorable weather. The total turnover for the week was 223,700 *dan* of American cotton. The spot cotton business in the market was quite quiet, with various factories purchasing 9,360 *dan* and firms purchasing 4,080 *dan* of Yao cotton. 6,646 bales of Yao cotton arrived. The bales purchased by each manufacturer and firm are recorded below:

Grain: Downriver Rice Market Turns Weak After Sunny Weather 104

Zhabei: Yesterday, the inland supply came from over ten sources. Market sales trended sluggish. The inventory downriver was estimated at over thirty sources. The North Guild had decent purchasing interest in broken *geng* rice, and the high price barely held its original level. Medium grades were generally weaker by one or two *jiao*. The common overall price was around 10.70 yuan. Since the weather cleared, market sentiment has gradually become bearish, because the new rice in the four districts will soon be harvested and enter the market, and the future supply is expected to become abundant. Therefore, cargo owners were eager to sell, and the market atmosphere became unfavorable. Dongxin *geng* rice continued to arrive one after another, and various factories showed a strong interest in sales, and the price slightly recovered by half a yuan, opening at around 18 yuan. The situation for thin-husked rice was flat. The goods arriving in Shanghai were extremely minimal. The price standard was similar to that of *geng* rice, and the overall trend was also flat and weak. The supply of new-crop *kejian* rice was abundant, and the cost of this cargo was extremely low. According to recent telegrams, the cost in Jiangsu was no more than 13 yuan. Therefore, the profit of merchants transporting this time was no less than that of foreign rice this spring. So once the market trended soft yesterday, it immediately shortened by two or three *jiao*. The top grade was only around 14 yuan. The evaluation and price reduction for middle grades was even greater, and the market was about to loosen. As for new *canjian* rice, it was available at times and not available at others. Although new rice had been seen, it was still difficult to connect and could only arrive in small quantities. The price of each grade followed the trends of foreign rice and *geng* and *kejian* rice. The white rice market was sluggish, and both the restaurant and brewing markets were watching. The overall market was not very prosperous, with only middle grades shortening by a small amount.

South Shanghai: Yesterday, not much rice arrived from downriver. The purchasing interests of this street varied. Top-grade *geng* rice was in short supply and had few arrivals, so any occasional arrivals saw excellent sales, and the situation was brisk. However, common old *geng* rice from Suzhou and other places was rarely inquired about. Although the supply was thin, the market sentiment softened greatly due to the clearing weather, so the market shortened by about two *jiao*. Dongxin *geng* rice and new *geng* rice from the south route were weak by two or three *jiao*, and the price ranged from 17.5 to 18 yuan. The stockpiles of thin-husked rice from the producing areas were sold off in batches, because the new cargo was about to arrive abundantly, so the selling atmosphere was brisk, and the price also trended weak by half a *qian*. However, this cargo has not been much in Shanghai recently, and most of the supply is still on the way, so a sharp reduction still had to wait a little longer. Yin yuan exchange was rare and sales were light, and the situation was generally flat.

Sugar Market: 3,500 Bags of Coarse Grain White Sugar Discharged 105

Yesterday, news from the sugar market production area indicated that due to it being Sunday, there were no telegrams. The Municipal Council market planning session revealed that the buying interest in Dutch sugar, specifically Grade 24 coarse grain white sugar, remained quiet. Ordinary goods were priced at 8.2 to 8.21 taels, with few transactions. New goods, those with coarse grains and high color, were priced up to 8.23 taels, but attracted even less attention. The market for medium grain white sugar remained the same as before, with sluggish activity. Japanese sugar with the "M" mark was traded at 8.15 taels, "YT" mark at 8.1 taels, "HS" mark at 8.05 taels, and "YP" mark at 8.1 taels. Transactions were dwindling. Although prices did not rise or fall compared to the previous day, the market felt particularly listless. Various foreign firms were selling off long-term Dutch sugar coarse grain white sugar. China Merchants sold 3,500 bags of coarse grain white sugar for October shipment at a price of 6.05 Dutch currency. As a result, shipments were fully opened. They offered to sell November shipments for 6 Dutch currency, but the firms' interests were weaker, leading to no transactions.

Silk and Tea: Ningfeng Rayon Sales Brisk, Supply Exhausted 106

Later Batch of Goods Offered at 107.5 Taels

Rayon is currently in a period of brisk sales, with demand from various manufacturers increasing. This is because all sectors welcome rayon products. Currently, ordinary goods are selling for 110.2 taels per 100 pounds, which is more popular than higher-end goods priced at 140-150 taels. The Ningfeng No. 4 blue "Ning" brand is in high demand from manufacturers and sells very well in the market. Currently, customers have searched and bought up all stock, and the supply in Shanghai is about to be exhausted. Consequently, asking prices have soared, rising by more than ten taels. (Previously, the market price was only 112.5 taels per 100 pounds.) Now, the asking price is 107.5 taels, and it is said that there is still an empty market.

Last Week's Silk Market Extremely Sluggish 107

Japanese Silk Sold at Low Prices, Chinese Silk Uninquired

European Sales Extremely Weak, Chinese Merchants Generally Pessimistic

Last week, silk transactions by foreign firms in this port were nearly exhausted. Since the economic downturn in European and American markets, silk mills have been trying to reduce costs and have no interest in purchasing expensive raw materials. The consumption of rayon has surged. Japanese silk merchants, due to an oversupply of cocoons and a thick stock of silk, took the opportunity to sell at low prices. Shanghai Chinese silk merchants complained that the prices were too high, and almost no one inquired. Spot and future silk in New York and Lyon saw few transactions. New autumn cocoons from Hangzhou and Shaoxing in Zhejiang Province have entered the market, and a good harvest is expected. However, silk prices are expected to be high, comparable to spring cocoons. The Jiaxing and Huzhou regions are also starting silkworm rearing, and cocoon purchasing personnel from various silk mills have begun to depart. Last week, European sales of spot silk were extremely weak, and Chinese silk merchants were generally pessimistic. Overseas silk prices continued to weaken, with prices quoted but no actual sales. Local News

Commemorating the Premier's First Uprising Tomorrow 119

丨The Municipal Executive Committee Holds a Commemorative Meeting丨

Location: Republic Road, Gonghe Cinema

Time: September 9th, 9:00 AM

Tomorrow (the 9th) marks the anniversary of the Premier's first uprising. The Shanghai Special Municipal Party Department has actively prepared in advance and specifically set 9:00 AM on that morning to convene people from all walks of life for a commemorative meeting. Party departments at all levels, various agencies, and organizations must send four representatives to participate. Details have been reported in this newspaper. The meeting location was originally set at the Xiaoximen Youth Propaganda Group but has now been changed to the Gonghe Cinema on Republic Road. A letter to all comrades will also be issued, stating that thirty-six years ago today, the revolutionary party led by the Premier launched its first uprising in Guangzhou. More than seventy revolutionary comrades sacrificed their blood. Although the revolutionary plan, carefully managed for many years, was completely exposed due to this failure, this unprecedented great undertaking spread to countries at home and abroad, shaking the numb Chinese nation and awakening the sleeping people of the whole country.

The Understanding and Efforts Due for the Commemoration of (September 9th) 120

1. In the autumn of 1894 of the Gregorian calendar, corresponding to the 20th year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty, the Sino-Japanese War erupted. The Qing forces suffered repeated defeats, the navy was completely annihilated, and the defensive barriers were entirely lost. Beijing and Tianjin were in imminent danger, and the people's hearts were filled with extreme indignation. The Premier, unwilling to see the nation in peril and the people suffering, along with three or five comrades including Deng Yin'nan, returned from overseas to Hong Kong. In the spring of the following year, they established the Revive China Society, planning to seize Guangzhou as a revolutionary base. The uprising was scheduled for September 9th but was unfortunately leaked, and firearms were seized by the Guangzhou customs. Lu Haodong, Qiu Si, and Zhu Guiquan, who were the first to sacrifice themselves for the revolution, died as a result. The Premier had no choice but to flee to Japan with Zheng Shiliang. This was the Premier's first uprising.

2. The Premier's first uprising held extremely significant meaning in terms of national, political, and social aspects. The revolutionary embryo of the Three Principles of the People gradually developed with this uprising. In the national aspect, the Premier witnessed the corruption of the Qing government and the nation's peril, and felt the revitalization and prosperity of advanced countries. He knew that without striving for a national movement, there was no way to save China from danger and destruction. In the aspect of people's rights, he deeply resented the oppression suffered by the entire nation, both internally from autocracy and externally from the trampling of the great powers. He knew that without overthrowing the fatuous and autocratic Qing government, it would be impossible to reform politics and promote civil rights. In the aspect of people's livelihood, imperialists, relying on their political advantages as a backing for economic aggression, had almost completely destroyed China's agricultural economy. The Qing government only knew how to oppress the people and did not know how to seek remedies. Therefore, unless this fatuous and corrupt government was overthrown, the problem of the people's livelihood would be impossible to resolve. Thus, the Premier's first uprising already contained the spirit of the three major revolutions: nationalism, democracy, and people's livelihood.

3. Based on the above, in commemorating the Premier's first uprising, (1) we must recognize that the Premier's first uprising was the first endeavor of the Chinese nation to promote national spirit, restore national freedom, and save the nation from destruction; (2) we must recognize that the Premier's first uprising was the beginning of the national revolution, not a struggle for power by heroes and chivalrous figures of a feudal society (taking over the dynasty), and that it opened a new era in Chinese history; (3) we must recognize that the Premier's first uprising was a great revolution to save the people from suffering and was launched out of an unwillingness to sit idly by and watch the people's livelihoods be cut off.

4. In commemorating the Premier's first uprising, the efforts we should make are: (1) We must overthrow imperialism and abolish unequal treaties because the Premier's first uprising was against the aggression and oppression of imperialists, and the reason why imperialists can invade and oppress our nation is because they use unequal treaties as a shield. (2) We must eliminate the remnants of feudalism and strive for revolutionary construction. Since the overthrow of the Qing Dynasty, warlords within the country have been constantly fighting for power, and the corruption of politics and the suffering of the people's livelihood are even worse than in the Qing Dynasty. In the fifteenth year, our party launched the Northern Expedition, relying on the efforts of the officers and soldiers and the support of the people, and unified the country in less than three years. Unexpectedly, new and old warlords rebelled one after another. The Gui faction and Tang rebels were just put down when Yan Feng and Wang rebels colluded with each other to cause chaos in Beiping and colluded with communist bandits to ravage Hunan and Jiangxi and poison the people. Therefore, in commemorating the Premier's first uprising, we should continue the revolutionary spirit of the Premier's first uprising, support the central government, assist in suppressing the rebellion, thoroughly annihilate the counter-revolutionary forces of Feng, Wang, etc., and permanently consolidate the foundation of peaceful unification, thereby realizing the Premier's legacy of saving the country and the people.

Slogans: (1) To commemorate (September 9th), we must abide by the Premier's teachings. (2) To commemorate (September 9th), we must overthrow imperialism. (3) To commemorate (September 9th), we must abolish all unequal treaties. (4) To commemorate (September 9th), we must strive for political tutelage, promote civil rights, and consolidate the foundation of democratic governance. (5) To commemorate (September 9th), we must promote unification, develop production, and solve the problem of people's livelihood. (6) Overthrow Feng, Wang, and other rebels who betray the party and harm the country and the people. (7) Overthrow the Communist Party, the Reorganization Clique, and the Western Hills Conference faction. (8) Long live the success of the National Revolution! (9) Long live the Chinese Kuomintang! (10) Long live the Republic of China!

Propaganda Department of the Shanghai Special Municipal Party Headquarters of the Chinese Kuomintang. In the history of the Chinese Revolution, [the September 9th Uprising] opened a new epoch. We analyze the causes and consequences of this event to give our comrades a simple report. As a result of the modern industrial revolution and political changes, brutal imperialism has extended its aggressive iron fist from Europe to the entire world. Significant events include the partitioning of Africa, the occupation of Australia, the destruction of India, and the annexation of small countries in Southeast Asia and the islands of Southeast Asia. Among countries with colored people outside of the white race of Europe, except for Japan, which was spared from danger due to the Meiji Restoration, no other country was not gradually weakening or disappearing. In this situation, China's domestic politics were mediocre, and the Manchu Qing's harshness was unbearable for the people. Moreover, economically and politically, China was dominated by imperialist powers. In addition, after strengthening itself, Japan also followed the European powers and launched attacks on the Asian continent. The Chinese nation was surrounded on all sides and was on the verge of destruction day by day. However, the state of the country was like this,

those in power were still ignorant and foolish, holding the attitude of "rather give to foreign friends than to domestic slaves." The general public was still under double oppression and did not dare to express even a groan. At that time, Mr. Sun Yat-sen, the Premier, was in this agricultural feudal society that had been left for thousands of years, and which was also a nation that deeply loved peace and was weak in resistance. Every day he heard slogans of "worshiping emperors" and "respecting the sacred." It was not only difficult to stir up the rage of revolution, but it was also difficult to arouse the sentiment of revolution. However, the Premier always wanted to shout the slogans of "overthrow autocracy" and "establish a republic" to promote revolution in this muddled society, regardless of all high pressure and intimidation, and regardless of all criticism and ridicule. He not only advocated revolution but also put it into practice, doing things that the world had never done before. As a result, the great feat of the first uprising was created. Although this event failed because of the exposure of the transport of weapons, the tide of revolution has since surged and cannot be contained. Shi Jianru's bombing of the Governor-General's Office of Guangdong and Guangxi, Huang Kecqiang's uprising in southern Hunan, Xu Xilin and Qiu Jin's uprisings in the Yangtze River, as well as the battles of Huizhou, Chaozhou, Guangzhou Huanghuagang, Qinlian Zhennanguan Xiaosihukou, and even the success of the Xinhai Revolution, one after another, were all inspired by the spirit of the Premier's first uprising. Without the fact of the Premier's first uprising, there would have been no successive and continuous revolutionary movements, let alone the success of Xinhai. Even the fact that our party has what it has today may have been facilitated by the first uprising. Comrades, we can know that the Premier was not a rich man. He had no money. He was not a feudal warlord. He had no men and horses or weapons. All he had was a strong and resolute, indomitable spirit, and a compassionate and broad personality that embraced everything. The martyrs who sacrificed their lives for the first uprising, such as Lu Haodong, Zhu Guijin, Qiu Si, and more than seventy other comrades, had the heroic revolutionary act of sacrificing themselves to be loyal to their cause. We absolutely recognize that the Premier's first uprising was the first endeavor of the Chinese nation to promote national spirit, restore national freedom, and save the nation from destruction. The Premier's first uprising was a revolutionary movement to promote civil rights and transform politics. The Premier's first uprising was a revolutionary strategy to solve economic problems in a Chinese society without the rudiments of capitalism, so as to achieve a situation where the people were adequately nourished. Now the Premier has passed away. The Republic of China, which was left behind by the first uprising, is even worse than the Manchu Qing Dynasty because of the domestic warlords' competition for power, political corruption, and the people's livelihood. In the fifteenth year, our party inherited the Premier's legacy and launched the Northern Expedition. For three years, it unified China. However, although the old warlords collapsed, new warlords rebelled one after another. Tang, Gui, Feng, and Yan successively raised troops. Wang Jingwei, a hypocrite who repeatedly changed his mind and called himself a follower of the Premier, sold his personality in order to develop his personal leadership and control desires, (recognized the enemy as his father), and now stumbles into the door of Yan Xishan, the local emperor of Shanxi (wagging his tail and begging for mercy) (respectfully listening to his holy instructions). He also put together a group of bored politicians, frustrated bureaucrats, and Western Hills Conference members who undermined the party's discipline, colluded with communist party greedy and unprincipled reorganization cliques, and held an enlarged meeting in the style of a "post-disaster meeting" in an attempt to subvert the party's orthodoxy. He also instigated communist bandits to ravage Hunan and Jiangxi, endanger our party and the country, and poison the people. All kinds of crimes are difficult to describe. As for Wang Jingwei's past acts of rebelling against the party and the country, they were already very absurd. Comrades, your understanding of him is very clear. Because he is good at flowery words and pretends to be famous, young people with weaker wills are unknowingly anesthetized by him, and think that he does not choose means to achieve his goals, and that his feelings are sincere and he should be forgiven. However, if we look at the fallacies that Wang Jingwei released this time in Beiping, what he said about (political supremacy in agreement), (party affairs supremacy in public), what (promote the National Assembly), (popular movements should aim to assist local autonomy), (cancel the slogan of ruling the country by the party during the period of political tutelage), and admit (political societies of other political parties), etc., are so absurd that they cannot be added to. Wang Jingwei wanted to please the warlords, so there is no need to discuss it, but when we look back on the Premier's history of revolutionary struggle for more than forty years, and the earnest advice of the entire party's comrades, especially in today's anniversary of the first uprising, we cannot even try to understand him. The Communist Party destroyed our party. First, they wanted to destroy the history of our party. They once said, (the blood shed before the thirteenth year) (was all animal blood). Their insult to our party has reached the extreme. However, Wang Jingwei then echoed it. He said, (the party members before the thirteenth year were not revolutionary parties). This kind of outrageous words, he insulted the Premier and insulted the martyrs, is unforgivable. In the middle of the first uprising, recalling the martyrs who sacrificed for the party, Mr. Lu Haodong, Zhu Guiquan, Qiu Si, we should feel how they killed themselves to become benevolent, and follow the spirit of loyalty to the party and the country, to support the central government, lead the people, and declare war on Wang Jingwei, the rebel who betrayed the party and the country and insulted the martyrs. Comrades, the National Revolution has reached a new and at the same time the most serious period, because the reactionary forces, fearing that the revolution will succeed and have no place to accommodate themselves, are making their last struggle. Imperialists also want to take the opportunity to attack. When we commemorate the Premier's first uprising, we should deeply understand the Premier's will, eliminate the remnants of feudalism, strive for revolutionary construction, abolish unequal treaties, and overthrow imperialism, in order to consolidate the foundation of peaceful unification forever and realize the Premier's legacy of saving the country and the people.

Prior notice was given to various mass organizations to send personnel to participate, so a large number of attendees were present. Citywide Curfew Yesterday 122

Order Remained Quiet and Normal

Yesterday was the commemorative day of the September Seventh Incident. The Director of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Yuan Liang, had received an order from the Songhu Garrison Command to implement a special curfew, similar to the May 1st arrangements. After receiving the order, Director Yuan immediately instructed the district and team officers and police officers under his jurisdiction to deploy three shifts of guards at key locations within the territory, strictly enforcing security. He also instructed all inspectors and investigators from the bureau to go to various districts and stations to intensify inspection patrols. No incidents occurred. The prevention measures are summarized as follows:

The Public Concession Police Department, considering Nanjing Road to be a critical location, increased the deployment of Chinese and foreign patrol officers on the streets yesterday morning. Security was tight in an invisible manner. At around 10:00 AM, several dozen men near the intersection of Nanjing Road and Shanxi Road shouted slogans and distributed leaflets. They were dispersed by the arresting officers, and the Laozha Police Station detained one person.

The French Concession General Police Department's General Inspector Fei announced a special curfew starting at 8:00 AM yesterday. In addition to ordering all the heads of the police stations under its jurisdiction to increase the deployment of Western police officers, leading Chinese and Vietnamese police officers in teams to set off for strict patrols, they also ordered a large number of Western police officers to each lead five or six Chinese and Vietnamese police officers to the intersections of various roads on the border between the Chinese and French concessions to choose key areas for deployment. All the iron gates at Xieqiao, Ximen, Nanyang Bridge, and the area around Minguo Road were locked tightly, leaving only small doors on both sides of the sidewalk for passage. At the intersection of West Xinquiao Street, Zilaihuo Street, East Xinquiao Street, Zhengjia Muqiao Street, Mofang Street, Tianzhutang Street, and other locations on Aiduya Road, barbed wire frames were placed across the road, leaving only gaps for vehicles to pass. All the plainclothes detectives were also dispatched, patrolling in teams, strictly investigating and inspecting. In addition, the Great World Amusement Park was ordered to suspend performances during the day, and the iron gates were tightly closed until 7:00 PM in the evening, when ticket sales began.

South Shanghai: Yesterday, military and police protection was quite thorough. Starting at 6:00 AM, the Songhu Garrison Command ordered the 26th Regiment infantry patrol team and the motor vehicle patrol team of the Fifth Division to patrol back and forth at key locations along the Chinese and French concessions, strictly enforcing security. In addition to the extra patrols by the stations in each district, the Municipal Public Security Bureau also sent security teams in cars to patrol the main roads in conjunction with the military police. Male and female investigators from the Inspectorate also collaborated with the station police in each district to inspect anyone with suspicious appearances. At 7:00 PM, passwords were issued, and all Chinese businesses along Fahua Minguo Road closed their doors and locked up before 9:00 PM. Electric lights were dim, and the scene was unusually solemn. It was said that traffic was completely cut off late at 12:00 AM.

Zhabei: In Zhabei, in addition to the extra shifts of police officers yesterday, traffic was not cut off.

West Shanghai: Ren, the district chief of the Sixth District of Caojiadu, announced a special curfew yesterday. In addition to issuing orders to all the police stations under his jurisdiction to increase the number of shifts and patrols, he also ordered Inspector Xu to lead all the head police and police officers in teams to set off and patrol back and forth on Bailinan Road, Jifei'er Road, Laobosen Road, and Kangnaotuo Road. Special attention was paid to the vicinity of various factories. In other areas, such as Wujiaochang, additional police officers were deployed. In addition, Liu Shaoqing, the leader of the detective team, led the detectives to conduct strict inspections in shifts. If there was anything suspicious, it had to be inspected once.

The Price Stabilization Committee Urges Payment of Donations 123

The Shanghai Municipal Rice and Grain Price Stabilization Committee yesterday sent separate letters to each member urging them to submit donation books. The letter stated, "Our committee previously stated that running the price stabilization program required a large amount of funds. If we do not widely gather the strength of the masses, it will be difficult to overcome this obstacle. We previously requested the Social Affairs Bureau to invite you to be a member of our committee to raise funds and attached donation books to request your solicitation. Since the commencement of operations, calculations show that the deficits are not small, and the donations received are still difficult to compensate. Now that the end is not far off, we kindly request your committee members to quickly solicit donations to meet the urgent needs. We hope that you will submit the donations you have raised along with the donation books by September 10th. If there are any donors who have not paid, please indicate the donor's name, donation amount, and address so that we can send personnel to collect."

Opinions on Promoting Domestic Goods 125

First, It is Necessary to Elucidate the Principles of Production

Compile Textbooks on Domestic Goods Production

The Industrial and Commercial Visit Bureau of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce believes that in order to persuade citizens to use domestic goods, it seems appropriate to collect teaching materials in geography and natural science subjects in primary and secondary school textbooks, classify and compile them, in order to cultivate the habit of citizens loving and using domestic goods. It has submitted a report to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce, requesting the Ministry of Education to review and handle it. The original text of the Bureau is recorded as follows: It is believed that to restore social customs, we rely on the power of education to remind us, and advocating the use of domestic goods is especially helpful for cultivating the spirit of rectitude. The way our country has established itself since ancient times, what is called the six treasuries and three affairs, is nothing more than following the constant track of producing more and consuming less, so as to use production to relieve national needs, and to teach the people about local products, which coincides with the Premier's advocacy of the Principle of People's Livelihood. Since the eastward expansion of European civilization, our compatriots have been so fascinated by material civilization that they have almost abandoned the good methods and intentions of producing more and consuming less in our country. All four aspects of clothing, food, housing, and transportation compete to use imported goods. At its extreme, even superior American goods and substitutes for domestic products are ignored. Recently, although the government has issued a clear order that service personnel in all agencies use domestic goods as a model for the people, who knows that although the order is grand, listening to it is finally indifferent.

Page 14

The officials in the agencies are still like this, and the general society is even more predictable. This advocacy is followed by that, and a prairie fire ensues. The upper class influences the lower class, and it is like the wind blowing on the grass. However, at this time when it is difficult to reverse the situation, we must consider a method of silent transformation. We have checked the textbooks of various primary and secondary schools in various countries, and geography textbooks and natural science textbooks are compiled with detailed descriptions of the local products of the country, so that children can learn about the way to love and use domestic goods and save money. Our country has a vast territory and abundant resources, and the local products of each province are diverse and abundant. Although the degree of industrialization has not yet been developed for a while, the original famous products have not been promoted and developed. If we can, from the educational aspect, order various bookstores to collect and compile all domestic goods production businesses into secondary school textbooks and promote them, so that children can learn about them and rely on their perceptions to cultivate a habit of loving and using domestic goods. Although the efforts are small, the results will be great. The Bureau has always done its best to advocate and promote the advocacy of domestic goods in publications. Recently, we have carefully discussed with teachers and made a contribution to our humble knowledge. We have submitted it to you for your listening. If it is adopted, please consult with the Ministry of Education for review. The reason for collecting domestic goods production and local products in textbooks, so as to achieve the effect of enlightening cultivation, is it appropriate? We hereby respectfully submit it to you for your review and implementation.

Shanghai South District Defense Corps Inspected Yesterday 126

Sun Baorong's Address

The Shanghai Municipal Shanghai District Defense Corps, since it was ordered to be reorganized, has completed its registration and was inspected at the Nanshi Stadium at 2:00 PM yesterday. Sun Baorong, Chairman of the Rectification Committee, personally went to the venue to inspect each team. After the inspection, he gave an address, the words of which are as follows:

In the Defense Corps, there are corps commanders, corps deputy commanders, team leaders, platoon leaders, and squad leaders. It seems that the ranks are divided a lot, but the Defense Corps is an armed group organized by the people to defend their own places. Therefore, although the ranks are divided, the corps commander and the corps members are no different from family fathers and sons. I am the standing member of the Rectification Committee, and also one of the Defense Corps members, so in terms of rank, I am an official, and in terms of the corps, it is like a family talking. So I believe that today's words are very kind and very sincere. If you listen to my words and do what I say, you will probably not be wrong. Why does the Defense Corps need to be reorganized and inspected? Why didn't it need to be reorganized and inspected in the past, but now it needs to be reorganized and inspected? There is a reason for this. In the past, the Nanshi Defense Corps was called the First Corps, the Beishi was called the Second Corps, and Pudong was called the Third Branch Corps. The remaining townships also had corps and branch corps. Then, in terms of a team, some had more and some had less. The most had more than 300 members, and the least had as few as 20 or 30 members. What order should Nanshi be the first, and Beishi should be the second? What standard should a certain district be a corps and a certain district be a branch corps? What circumstances should there be such a big difference? To sum it up in one sentence, it is that each is self-governing and there is no organization. The Rectification Committee is responsible for the mission of rectification, so it naturally pays attention to the organization. Therefore, after the meeting, it sent members to investigate in various townships, consult with local people, exchange opinions, and deliberate on the situation, and set a standard table, which was reported to the Municipal Government. The Municipal Government then underwent a detailed review before approving and issuing it together with the funds for each district corps. Now it is stipulated that the quota for a team is 108 members. The Nanshi Defense Corps was reorganized from twelve teams to nine teams. As long as you count on your fingers, you will know that the Nanshi Corps has 972 members. By extension, if you know how many teams there are in Beishi and various townships, you will know how many members they have. This is the reason for the reorganization and inspection. Among you 972 people, no matter who you are, you are responsible for defending the local area. You must understand the meaning of the Defense Corps, implement the principles of the Defense Corps. When you become a member of the Defense Corps, you are serving the local area. In other words, the people of the local area rely on our Defense Corps to protect them. How great is our responsibility, how glorious is our reputation, how noble is our personality. Under the guidance of the Premier's Three Principles of the People and the legacy of mutual assistance, especially in Shanghai, where all kinds of people are mixed together, good and bad are not uniform, and all kinds of reactionary elements, what kind of communists, kidnappers, secret thieves, and robbers are everywhere. If you are not careful, you can disrupt the local tranquility. We must work hard to eradicate these human parasites. We must use all our strength to prevent the restlessness of these bad elements in the areas we protect, so that the people in our protected areas can enjoy peace, not suffer losses, and not be panic-stricken. Then the three words "Defense Corps" will be resounding, and you will not be a member of the Defense Corps in vain. To put it another way, Shanghai has always been mentioned in the same breath as the military, police, and corps. The army is for foreign enemies, the police maintain public order, and only our Defense Corps, although its task is to assist the military and police, its nature is no different from that of a business corps. It is entirely for the protection of itself. The government should also send personnel and allocate funds to manage and rectify us. Then our corps members should fulfill some obligations, and what they eat is nothing. Therefore, as a corps member, one, you must absolutely obey orders, two, you must effectively defend the local area, three, you must abide by discipline, four, you must recognize your responsibilities, and five, you must intensify training. If you have not done the above five points, you must hurry to go in this direction. If you have already done it, you must continue to work hard and never give up. What I have taught today is here, and what I hope is also here. That's all.

County Public Safety Bureau Requests Advance Payment of Back Wages 127

Totaling Approximately 20,000 Yuan for Five Months

The Shanghai County Public Safety Bureau, citing the non-payment of wages for nearly five months, which has severely impacted the ability of police officers to sustain themselves, yesterday formally requested the county government to temporarily advance funds to alleviate their financial hardship. The submitted document is as follows:

"Subject: Urgent Request for Allocation of Long-Overdue Wages to Alleviate the Financial Distress of Police Officers.

It has come to our attention that the salaries of the police officers under the jurisdiction of this bureau have been in arrears for four and a half months, starting from the latter half of January of this year, with only one month's worth of wages being paid by the former County Magistrate during his tenure. Subsequently, only a small amount of food allowance was disbursed. Most of these police officers come from impoverished families and rely entirely on these salaries to sustain their livelihoods. Since the onset of wage arrears, they have exhausted all means of pawnage and borrowing, enduring hardships that are difficult to describe. Their forbearance and dedication to service are due not only to the repeated encouragement from the County Magistrate but also to the hope that the arrears will be cleared in due course, thereby providing relief. However, as the delay has persisted for an extended period, this matter of wage arrears remains unresolved, causing them to feel anxious and restless day and night. Should this situation continue indefinitely, it will become a lingering issue, jeopardizing the officers' livelihoods and making it difficult to remain silent. The bureau chief is constantly questioned by his subordinates, and he is at a loss for an answer. Previously, this bureau received a clear directive from your esteemed office, which was forwarded from the provincial government, to dispatch personnel to jointly request the government to settle the outstanding debts. The original intention was to clear the wage arrears. Now, several months have passed, and this bureau has repeatedly petitioned for an advance payment, pending the resolution of disputes between the province and the city, before reimbursement. To date, no resolution has been reached, and the subordinates are in dire straits. This document is hereby submitted to your esteemed office for review, humbly requesting that you forward it to the relevant authorities for approval, so that it can be disseminated for compliance."

Biographical Notes on Contemporary Figures 128

Wang Chonghui, President of the Judicial Yuan, and Wei Daoming, Mayor of Beijing, departed for Beijing yesterday at 1:45 PM on a special express train.
