U.S. Transport Ship Chaumont Departs Shanghai 130

Carrying Over a Hundred Marines and Sailors

The Continental Daily reports that the U.S. transport ship Chaumont departed Shanghai last night (the 6th) and will return to the United States via Hong Kong, Manila, Guam, and Honolulu. The ship is carrying three hundred sailors and one hundred and fifty marines from the Fourth Regiment, whose terms of service in the Far East have expired, back to their home country. Additionally, it is transporting many sick soldiers from various ships in Shanghai and the Yangtze River to the naval hospital in the Philippines for convalescence.

County Government Raises Treasury Bonds to Settle Payments 131

The Shanghai County Government has received an order from the provincial government to raise 60,000 yuan in customs treasury bonds, which has subsequently been reduced to 40,000 yuan. The order mandates that the county government make every effort to raise the funds, and if the full amount cannot be raised, it is permitted to temporarily borrow funds from the approved two-yuan surcharge on tribute rice for settlement, to be repaid upon the collection of winter tribute rice. Upon receiving the order, County Magistrate Yan immediately began actively raising funds. Given the urgent need for customs treasury bonds for military expenditure, it was agreed with Director Wang of the Finance Bureau that, in addition to the 1,500 yuan already remitted, an additional 3,500 yuan would be raised and remitted, for a total of 5,000 yuan. It is also reported that the raising of cigarette treasury bonds has been temporarily suspended by order.

Progress of the South Seas Inspection Team for Domestic Goods 132

Meeting to be Held Tomorrow

The Shanghai National Products Factories United Association sent a letter to various factories yesterday, stating: "Gentlemen, at the factory representatives meeting held on the 4th of this month, due to the limited number of registrations for the Singapore trade fair, it was decided to reorganize into the South Seas Islands Inspection Team to facilitate the carrying of samples to Hong Kong, Annam, Saigon, Singapore, Penang, Java, Sumatra, Siam, and other places for extensive promotion. The round trip is expected to take about two months. It is planned to travel by postal ship, and if more than ten people register, round-trip tickets can be purchased at 75% of the original price. The cost for each factory to send one representative, including travel and other expenses, is estimated at 1,000 yuan. The China Industrial Factory, China Enamel Factory, Watson Electric Factory, and Golden Rooster Necktie Company were appointed as preparatory committee members on the spot. The departure is tentatively scheduled for November 1st. Your esteemed factory had previously registered its willingness to participate. A meeting is scheduled for 2:00 PM on the 8th of this month (Monday) at this association in Jiu'an Lane to discuss the implementation plan. We kindly request that your esteemed factory send a representative to attend and discuss the matter. Your prompt attention to this matter is greatly appreciated."

Industrial Products Testing Laboratory

Addition of Textile Testing 133

The Municipal Industrial Products Testing Laboratory in Shanghai (address: 4 Hehe Lane, Xiafei Road; telephone: 37263), which has been in operation for the past two years since its establishment, has handled a total of two hundred and several tens of cases involving testing and research commissioned by various manufacturers in the city, earning widespread trust and a high reputation in the community. This year, it has added textile testing facilities, ordered equipment from abroad, and dispatched personnel to various factories to collect products. Those that have been successively sent to the laboratory include: velvet from Tongcheng Textile Company; cotton and silk stockings from Shanghai Textile Factory and Tongji Hosiery Factory; silk fabrics from Jinyun, Meiya, Wuhua, and other silk factories; fabrics of various colors from Dafeng, Lixin, Hongxin, Sanxin, and other dyeing and weaving factories; coarse cloth from Yong'an, Hengfeng, Housheng, Zhentai, and other textile companies; cotton fabrics of various colors from Samsung Cotton Iron Company; various undershirts, health shirts, and trouser materials from Wuhe Textile Factory; canvas from Huacheng Canvas Factory; Beichou silk from Kenhuang Huachou Silk Factory; and woolen fabrics from Zhanghua Dahua Woolen Factory, totaling over three hundred pieces. Others are currently being collected by the Machine-Made National Products Factories United Association, the Silk Fabric Trade Association, the Knitting Industry Trade Association, and others. The ordered machinery has gradually arrived and been installed. Testing is expected to begin soon. At the same time, it is planned to collect products from various foreign countries for similar testing to identify their strengths and serve as a model for improving national products. Any weaving factory in the city wishing to determine the quality, strength, or color fastness of its products (cloth, silk, wool, velvet, gabardine, stockings, undershirts, health shirts, etc.), or to compare the quality with similar imported products, may commission the laboratory to conduct testing and issue certificates in accordance with the laboratory's regulations. Furthermore, any government agency, school, or individual purchasing clothing materials, woolen fabrics, blankets, etc., wishing to determine their quality or to verify whether delivered goods conform to samples, may also engage the laboratory for testing at a very low cost.

Recent Developments at China Merchants Steam Navigation Company 134

Requesting the New Acting General Manager to Take Office. Cai Ziping, the acting General Manager of China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, sent a telegram to Li Zhonggong, the newly appointed General Manager, who has already arrived in Beijing, requesting instructions from Minister Wang regarding the reorganization of the company. Cai reported that during his tenure as acting General Manager, the case involving the San De Tang was handled to the point of discussing the purchase of the warehouse property and the renewal of the wharf lease, thus avoiding the enforcement of the French court's judgment. Arrears in salary for all employees have also been paid for one month. All procedures have been handled clearly, and he is awaiting Li's arrival in Shanghai to prepare for the handover. As he is eager to hand over the responsibilities, he telegraphed Beijing, urging General Manager Li to take office as soon as possible. It is reported that Li is discussing with Minister Wang and others in Beijing issues such as financial measures and the nationalization of the company's operations. He will come to Shanghai after the discussion.

Construction Temporarily Suspended. The construction of Jinliyuan Warehouse No. 15, which began during Zhao Tieqiao's tenure, involved demolishing the old warehouse and building a new-style warehouse to develop transportation. The company's land in the Nanshi area was also to be redeveloped into new-style commercial buildings. Recently, as the commencement of construction of these two projects was approaching, General Manager Cai issued an order to temporarily suspend the construction work on both sites, pending the arrival of the new General Manager to the company before construction can proceed.

Current Operating Vessels. The company's upper Yangtze River steamer Emei, due to damage requiring repair, will arrive in Shanghai today. The ocean-going fleet has a large number of vessels in Hankou and Haizhou. Therefore, only five vessels are currently in operation.

Competition Plans. Shen Zhongyi and Li Yunliang, the chief and deputy of the Business Department, have a fundamental plan to reorganize and expand competition in the Yangtze River shipping industry to reclaim shipping rights lost to foreign companies. However, the Zhao case and the inability to maintain scheduled voyages have prevented its implementation. Recently, Shen and Li, given the lifting of the ban on rice transport on the Yangtze River, are taking advantage of this suspension of voyages to plan the implementation of expanded competition in upstream and downstream Yangtze River shipping. They are currently consulting with branch offices in various ports via telegram and letter, and are very busy.

Jiangsu Construction Department

Order to Investigate Electric Light Plants Established in Cities and Towns 135

The Shanghai County Government received an instruction from the Jiangsu Construction Department, stating: "Regarding the Electric Power Business plan submitted by the Construction Committee, the General Assembly resolved to expedite the establishment of electric light plants within cities. As the electric power business is of great importance, European and American countries have been developing it for fifty years and continue to invest their efforts without reservation. Our country is still in its infancy in this regard. Unless we make a concerted effort to catch up, we will not be able to meet the needs of the current century or achieve the goal of universal electrification. In addition to distributing the order, the original plan is hereby copied and sent to your department, instructing you to diligently follow the three steps of investigation, planning, and implementation, and to report the progress regularly for verification." This order is hereby forwarded, along with the original plan. Although the electric power business in our province has taken shape, there are still many counties, townships, and towns without electric light plants. It is imperative to actively promote and plan to achieve universal electrification. The method of implementation should begin with investigation. All county-level urban areas, cities, and towns suitable for establishing electric light plants should be thoroughly investigated as a basis for planning and implementation. In accordance with this order, the County Magistrate Yan, in addition to distributing the order, is hereby forwarding two copies of the investigation form, instructing the county's Construction Bureau to work with the heads of various districts to conduct investigations and report in accordance with the items listed in the form for verification. County Magistrate Yan has instructed the Construction Bureau to forward the documents to the district chiefs for compliance.

Trade Associations Must Be Formed If There Are More Than Seven Businesses in the Same Industry 136

Cannot Join the Chamber of Commerce as Individual Shops

Previously, the Municipal Chamber of Commerce was instructed by the Ministry of Industry and Commerce that shop members of the Chamber of Commerce must be members of a trade association if there are fewer than seven companies in the same industry within the same region. Otherwise, a trade association must first be organized, and representatives then sent to the Chamber of Commerce by the trade association. This regulation differs from the principle of the Chamber of Commerce Law decided by the Central Political Conference, which stipulates that even if businesses in the same industry meet the conditions for organizing a trade association, they are not required to do so. As there are conflicting opinions, a special request was submitted to the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for verification and instruction. The Chamber has now received a response from the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, stating: "Upon review, Article 2 of the Amended Implementing Regulations of the Industrial and Commercial Trade Associations Law stipulates that (when there are seven or more companies or firms in the same industry in the same region, they must organize a trade association in accordance with this law), etc. This order has been promulgated by the Ministry and must be followed accordingly, without the need for further inquiries. Please be informed of this ruling."

Salary Increase for Employees of Two Railways 137

Employees in various departments under the jurisdiction of the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations receive a salary increase once every year in January or July. The salary increase period for July of this year has arrived. Department heads have submitted lists to the Administration Division, requesting salary increases at different levels according to the established precedent. Director Liu has submitted the request to the Ministry, and the announcement is expected to be made soon. The salary increase issue for the police departments of the two railways has already been announced, instructing the police departments of various sections to comply. Section chiefs will receive an increase ranging from ten to seven yuan, depending on their rank. Those who have worked for less than one year will not receive an increase. Patrol officers will receive five yuan, patrol leaders two yuan, and patrolmen one yuan.

Freight Rates Remain at 6% 138

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations previously received the sixth edition of the new regulations for passenger and freight transport promulgated by the Ministry of Railways, scheduled to take effect on September 1st. The Traffic Department immediately instructed station staff to comply with the new regulations. It has now been learned that the new regulations for passenger and freight transport on the Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo line have already been implemented. However, the original freight rate for passenger baggage was 6% per kilogram per fifty kilometers. The newly issued sixth edition increases this rate by 1% to 7%. Now, with the approval of the Ministry, the freight rate for passenger baggage will remain at the old rate of 6%. The Traffic Department has telegraphed all relevant station staff to take note of this.

Citizens Association Urges British Firm to Compensate Insurance Premiums 139

The Citizens United Association sent a letter to the British firm Jardine Matheson, urging them to compensate the insurance premiums for the Hanlun Silk Weaving Factory in Hangzhou, stating: "Regarding the matter of notice, this association has received a telegram dated the 30th from the Zhejiang General Chamber of Commerce, stating that member Cao Shengming established the Hanlun Silk Weaving Factory in Hangzhou and insured it with the Shanghai British firm Jardine Matheson for 10,000 taels of silver. He holds two insurance policies: (1) 22 wooden jacquard looms, insured for 6,000 taels of silver, and other goods insured for 2,000 taels of silver; (2) business assets insured for 1,000 taels of silver and clothing insured for 1,000 taels of silver, totaling 10,000 taels. Unfortunately, on March 20th of this year, due to the negligence of a neighbor, a fire spread to the factory, completely destroying it and causing losses of over 27,000 yuan. Subsequently, Jardine Matheson entrusted the Louis Moore firm to conduct an on-site inspection in Hangzhou. Initially, they made excuses about unclear accounts, then insisted on copying the police station's fire investigation report for further discussion. Finally, they falsely claimed that the factory did not have 22 looms, even asserting that the factory had not been operating in recent years. Cao Shengming urgently sought the insurer to fulfill its responsibility and, in response to the accusations, provided evidence to refute each point. However, he was unable to gain the insurer's understanding. Eventually, Louis Moore, representing Jardine Matheson, declared that Jardine Matheson would not be responsible for the Hanlun insurance claim. Several months of negotiations yielded no results. It has been determined that the fire that destroyed the Hanlun Silk Weaving Factory was caused by others, and the factory was not intentionally or negligently at fault, as evidenced by the testimony of fireman Feng Zhao at the police station. Whether the factory was operating and how many looms it had can be easily verified and cannot be concealed by empty words. Jardine Matheson deliberately made unfounded accusations without providing any counter-evidence and delayed payment for several months, which is a breach of contract and good faith, tantamount to fraud, and undermines their insurance qualifications. We request your association to assist us in this matter." After discussion by the Specialized Committee of our association, it was generally agreed that the British firm Jardine Matheson should fulfill its obligation to pay the insurance claim for the Hanlun Silk Weaving Factory in Hangzhou and cannot make baseless accusations or shirk their credibility and responsibility. It was resolved to send a special letter of warning, requiring them to raise the full amount of 10,000 taels of silver within three days of receipt of the letter and compensate Cao Shengming of the Hanlun Silk Weaving Factory in Hangzhou for the overdue interest. Otherwise, the facts will be published in the newspaper, warning the Chinese public not to take out insurance with Jardine Matheson in the future. Those who have already taken out insurance and have not yet expired should cancel their policies as a penalty for Jardine Matheson's abandonment of credit and dereliction of responsibility. Accordingly, we hereby notify you and request that you investigate and respond within three days of receipt of this letter. Please do not neglect this important matter. To the British firm Jardine Matheson, from the Citizens United Association of the Shanghai Special District.

(2) The current supply of small pig intestines is very low, unlike previous years. However, foreign merchants are very strict when inspecting goods. It was resolved to request the Municipal Chamber of Commerce to send a telegram to the Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval.

Silk Filature Industry: In response to the truth about the import of Japanese cocoons and to alleviate this year's cocoon shortage, the Silk Filature Industry Trade Association sent a letter to the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, stating: "The Jiang, Zhe, and Wan provinces produced only a very meager spring and summer cocoon crop this year. Based on investigations, the total output is only a little over 200,000 piculs, which is nearly 45% less than in a bumper year. Most silk filatures, which rely on this raw material, are located in Shanghai. It is estimated that the supply of cocoons will be exhausted before the end of the year. As the silk market is depressed, silk filatures cannot make a profit. Once the raw material runs out and the factories are forced to shut down, over 100,000 workers will lose their jobs, and the families who rely on them for a living will also be in dire straits. If each family is estimated to have an average of three or four people, then 300,000 to 400,000 people will be plunged into poverty at the same time. After repeated consideration, the members of the silk filature industry want to uphold the principle of people's livelihood and show love and compassion. The only option is to adapt to the circumstances and seek a temporary relief measure. How can we idly talk about patriotism and watch these hundreds of thousands of people lose their livelihoods? As Japan has a bumper cocoon crop and is exporting them, it may be possible to set strict limits and purchase some dried cocoons to alleviate the temporary cocoon shortage. International trade is not prohibited by the government, and the import tariff rate for cocoons is set at 12.5% ad valorem. Moreover, in the past, when there was a surplus of Chinese cocoons, they were exported to Japan. Now that there is a shortage of Chinese cocoons, it is reasonable to purchase Japanese cocoons to provide relief. Cocoons are a raw material for silk production and are similar in nature to agricultural products such as rice, wheat, and cotton. Therefore, we request the Chairman of the Silk Cocoon General Association, Huang , to make preparations for the future, request instructions from the government, and ask for a one-year tax exemption to maintain the raw material costs in this declining silk market for necessary use in the future. It is reported that after the Customs Administration received instructions from the Ministry, it ordered the Silk Cocoon General Association to reduce the import tax on Japanese cocoons by 25% from October of this year to May of next year, with a limit of 60,000 piculs. This is to purchase Japanese cocoons to supplement the raw materials for silk reeling, thereby preventing the interruption of silk export trade and avoiding the loss of livelihoods for tens of thousands of workers. This is the course of events. Initially, when the Japanese sent cocoon samples, three or four silk filatures each purchased 10 to 20 catties of sample cocoons, some as many as 30 to 40 catties. After testing, the quality of the cocoons was found to be very good. Based on the reeling calculation, one picul of cocoons could produce one load of silk if 300 to 350 catties of cocoons were reeled. Thus, the load quota was set and a date was set for shipping to China. However, the Japanese silk manufacturers, out of jealousy, colluded with the cocoon merchants and forbade them from selling cocoons to Chinese merchants. Then, under the pretext of miscalculating the price, they suspended the shipment to China. This is also the truth about the widely circulated news that Japanese cocoons were shipped but not actually imported. We hereby report the facts truthfully."

Local News 2

Three Extortionists of 10,000 Yuan Arrested 143

Meeting Place Arranged at the Unified Hotel

Secret Plan: Detectives Posed as the Victim

Zhang Caigen and Two Others Arrested for Attempting to Get Rich

Banditry is rampant in Shanghai, and despite the rigorous investigations by the concession police authorities, they have not been able to curb the wave of crime. Yu Mingrui, a resident of the French Concession who deals in cotton yarn and has a modest but comfortable life, with lavish spending habits, attracted the attention of bandits. He recently received an extortion letter with very forceful language, stating that they needed military funds and demanding 10,000 yuan in cash, or else they would resort to illegal means. The letter also arranged a meeting at the Unified Hotel at 164 Edward Road, near Six Road, the night before last, with the letter serving as proof of identity. After receiving the letter, Yu Mingrui carefully examined the tone of the letter, deemed it rather dangerous, and immediately reported it to the French police for investigation. As the bandits' meeting place was in the Public Concession, the French police chief immediately reported it to Inspector Liu Shaokui of the General Police Station. Upon hearing this news, Liu, viewing it as a case of extortion against law-abiding citizens, and to eliminate bandits, immediately disguised himself and Chinese and foreign detectives and went to the Unified Hotel without making a sound. They pretended to be there to negotiate. As expected, someone came to talk to them, and they were arrested. As a result, three men, including Zhang Caigen from Tianjin, were arrested and taken back to the police station. It is reported that they will be transferred to the court for trial today.

Joint Suppression of Pirates in Da'an Port 144

Provincial Government Sends Junhe and Boxian Warships

Naval Department Sends Jingxing and Hu'e Warships

Da'an Port waters outside Wusong, where the sea meets land, is occupied by a large group of pirates who are creating a great disturbance, the details of which have been reported in this newspaper. Later, it was reported that the pirates there had been severely suppressed by the water and land police forces and had fled to the open sea. It is now known that the above news is not accurate. The pirates are now even more rampant than before, and the water and land police forces, due to their limited strength, have not yet found a way to suppress them. Zhang Han, the District Chief of the Fourth Water Police District of Wusong, fearing the potential for future trouble, went to the province a few days ago to meet with Provincial Governor Ye and Civil Affairs Director Hu to personally report on the rampant pirate situation and request instructions on suppression measures. The provincial government has now ordered Chapter Fengyi, captain of the Junhe warship stationed in the waters of Hupu and Baigang, and Wang Zijun, captain of the Boxian warship, to set off fully equipped with weapons, ammunition, and coal yesterday to Da'an Port waters. They will join forces with the patrol boats of the 17th and 18th teams of the Fourth Water Police District, as well as the Pingyang and Zhenhai gunboats under their command, to encircle and severely suppress the pirates. Meanwhile, the provincial government has sent a telegram to the Naval Department requesting it to send warships to assist in the suppression. According to information from the National Coastal Defense Command in Wusong, Wu Zhennan, the commander of the command, has received a telegram order from Chen Shaokuan, acting Minister of the Navy, to send the Jingxing gunboat and the Hu'e torpedo boat under his command to assist in the joint suppression.

Died Spitting Blood 145

Who was this person?

What illness was it?

Yesterday morning at eight o'clock, a man, appearing to be a coolie, approximately thirty years old, naked from the waist up, wearing only blue cloth trousers, barefoot and wearing straw sandals, was walking empty-handed along the section of Min Guo Road, east of Xin Qiao Street in the French Concession, in front of the entrance to Min Guo Li, when he suddenly collapsed. Fresh blood gushed from his mouth, and he died instantly. A patrolman discovered the scene and reported it to the Grand Clock Tower Police Station, who dispatched an investigator. They confirmed that the death was due to spitting blood caused by illness. Unable to find any family, the body was transported to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall autopsy room. After the investigator reported back to the police chief, they were instructed to photograph the body, and the hall was instructed to provide a coffin for burial, awaiting family identification at the tomb.

A Disastrous Marriage of the Qin and Xu Families 146

Love began, divorce ended

The sin of a deceitful matchmaker

Xu Hengtai, a stonemason living outside the Small South Gate on Sang Yuan Street, had only one daughter, nicknamed A'Nan, who was not particularly attractive. She was nineteen this year. Because she was an only child, her parents doted on her. Two years ago, Qin Yu Tai, a young master stonemason from the Lu Jia Bang Road bridge, Qin Genfu, who was twenty years old and unmarried, whose father had passed away, was introduced to her by his friend Wang Chunlin. Genfu and A'Nan fell in love. Wang told Qin that the Xu family was wealthy and she was an only child. He told A'Nan that the Qin family was rich and he was the only son. However, the opposite turned out to be true. But Qin and Xu had been in love for a long time, and last September, her belly grew large and could not be hidden. She was pregnant. Qin then demanded to marry her, but Xu Hengtai strongly opposed the illicit behavior. However, his wife, Xu Xu Shi, doted on her daughter and, because Qin and A'Nan had spoken of dying for love, they had no choice but to allow the marriage in November. However, two months after the marriage, she gave birth to a son. Unexpectedly, the love faded, and eventually they broke up. Recently, Xu A'Nan filed a lawsuit in the local court against Genfu, accusing him of seduction and abduction with the sole purpose of seizing her mother's family's property. Later, because she had borrowed money several times and her mother's family could no longer provide constant assistance, he realized they were not wealthy, and his attitude changed drastically, and he became abusive. On the sixteenth of last month, because of a private matter involving her mother-in-law, he became angry with her and forced her to drink medicine, causing her to fall into a coma. Later, neighbors sent her to Ye Lu Hospital for an injection and treatment, and she regained consciousness, discovering it was tranquilizer medicine, indicating he had intended to harm her. Furthermore, at the beginning of this month, she was beaten with a tree branch, leaving her covered in injuries. He then presented her with a rope and a knife, forcing her to choose one for suicide, leaving her with no way out, and she requested help. After the court confirmed that Xu A'Nan had indeed been injured, Qin Genfu was summoned yesterday. According to Qin, he did not beat her. He said that because she was often not at home, they did have arguments. As for the tranquilizer medicine, he was unaware of it and claimed she took it at her mother's house to harm him. After Prosecutor Wu verified the statements, he ordered Genfu to be detained pending investigation.

Father and Daughter Have Different Opinions 147

Wang Dehong Sues for His Daughter's Seduction

Wang Aidi Insists on Marrying Zhuang

Is she seventeen or twenty years old?

Wang Dehong, a Chinese constable No. 249 from the Harbin Police Station's San Dao Tou, accused Zhuang Ruinian, from Anhui, of seducing his daughter, Aidi. The case was heard in the Special District Local Court by Judge Cheng the day before yesterday afternoon. According to the plaintiff, his daughter, Aidi, is seventeen years old. Last year, when Zhuang was a patrolman at the Harbin Police Station, he lived in the same house with them. Seeing that his daughter had some looks, he seduced her and committed adultery, and then abducted her. He requested severe punishment. The defendant stated that he and the plaintiff had a good relationship because they worked in the same place, and that his daughter, Aidi, was also very close to him. On the tenth of last month, he was admitted to the hospital due to illness, and Aidi came to visit him from time to time. After he recovered, he was very grateful. One day, he went to the plaintiff's house and saw Aidi was going to a relative's house to celebrate, so the plaintiff asked him to accompany her. The rest of his statement mainly described his love affair with Aidi. Subsequently, Wang Aidi stated that she is twenty years old. The court noted that her reported age did not match her father's, so they asked her exactly how old she was. Aidi still claimed she was actually twenty years old. Her father said she was seventeen because she had previously accused someone of raping her. At that time, her father ordered her to say she was only seventeen years old when she appeared in court. If she said she was twenty years old, the judge would not prosecute the rape charge against person A. She obeyed her father's order. This case is different from the previous one, so she should tell the truth. However, the plaintiff insisted that his daughter was only seventeen years old, and there was a witness. Subsequently, a nearly fifty-year-old woman from Yancheng, Chu Jiangshi, was brought to court. She testified that she used to live in the same house with the plaintiff in Yu Deli in the French Concession. Aidi was born there. When she delivered the baby, it was in 1914, so she is really only seventeen years old. Her husband is currently Constable No. 1343. Judge Cheng further questioned Aidi, who insisted on her previous statement, saying that her father initially wanted to marry her to the defendant, but when he lost his job, he gave him the cold shoulder. Now, he wants her to remarry a Chinese constable No. 1039. Although she has not been to school, she knows the meaning of staying with one person until the end. Judge Cheng advised her not to be stubborn and to obey her father's orders. The girl said that since she had followed the defendant, she vowed not to change her mind, and especially did not want to go home with her father, as she would inevitably be abused. The court ordered the defendant and Aidi to be detained separately pending a further hearing.

Childhood Sweethearts Plan to Become a Family 148

The good news of Wu Jiusheng and Huang Xiaoya

Wu Mingkun, a resident of No. 6 Hefeng Road, Wusong, has a son named Jusheng, who is fifteen years old. The Huang family, who lives next door at No. 4, has a daughter named Xiaoya, who is the same age as Jusheng. Because of their close proximity, they often visited each other, were childhood sweethearts, and were very close. They often lingered in Xiaoya's room to play. The parents did not suspect anything because they were both minors. Little did they know that Jusheng already understood matters of the heart, and Xiaoya's love blossomed early. They had been secretly engaging in illicit affairs for some time, and Xiaoya was pregnant. The parents were completely unaware and in the dark. Recently, Mingkun recommended Jusheng to learn a trade in Shanghai, so he separated from Xiaoya. Although he was reluctant to leave, he dared not disobey his father's orders. The other day, the postman delivered a letter that was opened by Xiaoya's brother. It was sent by Jusheng to Xiaoya and mentioned their secret affair, saying she was more than two months pregnant, and asking what to do in the future. After Xiaoya's brother read it, he finally understood what was happening and told his father, scolding Xiaoya for being shameless. After being reprimanded, Xiaoya was filled with shame and anger and tried to hang herself, but fortunately, she was discovered before anything happened. It is now understood that both sets of parents feel that the matter has already reached this point, so there is no need to create further complications. They agreed to discuss marriage, so that the childhood sweethearts can finally become a family.

Zhao Xiuzhen Case Settled 150

Lawyer's Fees Become an Issue

The case of Zhao Xiuzhen, a dancer at the Da Dong Ballroom, suing Zhu Mintang for seduction and pregnancy, was approved by the Special District Court for summons and hearing. At the initial hearing, because the defendant did not appear, Judge Ge Zhitan adjourned the hearing to the sixth of this month for a further summons. However, a few days before the adjourned hearing, Zhu Mintang repeatedly went to Zhao's residence at No. 37 Fanshi Li on Murming Road to discuss settlement terms. A settlement was finally reached on the evening of the fifth. Zhu brought a letter withdrawing the private prosecution, which Zhao and her mother signed. Zhu then submitted the request for withdrawal. Therefore, outsiders only knew that the matter was settled, but the settlement terms were not announced. Although the case was withdrawn, another issue arose. When the case was settled, the lawyers for both parties were not consulted in advance. At the time, Zhao had hired lawyer Zhang Chongding, introduced by a Mr. Gu, and signed a retainer agreement, stating that the fees would be based on the highest amount stipulated in the Shanghai Bar Association's regulations, divided into civil and criminal parts. According to these regulations, the fees would be 1,500 yuan, payable upon completion of the case. Now that the case has been settled, Zhao believes that the lawyer's fees should be borne by the Zhu family. Negotiations have been ongoing through the original introducer for several days, and a resolution is expected on Sunday.

Luodian Bans Latrines 151

Yang Weixiong, the district chief of the fourth district (Luodian) of Baoshan County, and Gao Daoru, the chief of the third public security branch, recently discovered that each temple, every lunar new moon and full moon at dawn, were setting off earthen cannons, and each pig farm trading dates, were still on the lunar calendar's three, six, nine days, all are hindering the promotion of the national calendar. Therefore, yesterday they separately announced a strict ban, and ordered each pig farm, trade on the national calendar's three, six, nine days, to honor the calendar law. Furthermore, given that there are many latrines in the town, which not only harms hygiene, but also hinders the view, another announcement was issued banning them. The methods are recorded as follows: (1) The banning of latrines is divided into two types: those that are to be rebuilt within a time limit and those that are to be demolished within a time limit. (2) The decision to rebuild or demolish will be made jointly by this office and this bureau. (3) After a decision is made, it will be posted on the latrine and notified to the business owners. (4) Those who fail to comply within the time limit will be handled by the office and bureau, and all expenses will be borne by the craftsmen. For those that are demolished, the materials will be confiscated to offset the costs, and for those that are rebuilt, the business owners will pay the costs, otherwise they will be used as public latrines. (5) Those who are unwilling to rebuild but are willing to demolish will be allowed to do so, but must also complete the demolition within the time limit. (6) This is a local public welfare matter, and absolutely no pleading or delay will be tolerated.

Strange News of Lightning Strike at Yang Wang Temple in Baoshan 153

There was an old Yang Wang Temple inside the East Gate of Baoshan. Recently, it was intended to be converted into a fire station, a national arts research hall, and a primary school site. Therefore, many carpenters and artisans were hired to repair the temple buildings and completely renovate them, spending more than a thousand yuan in repairs. The project was about to be completed when, on the morning of the day before yesterday (the 6th) at about 9 o'clock, the sky suddenly became overcast, with lightning and thunder, followed by torrential rain. Suddenly, there was a loud crash, and the western half of the temple building immediately collapsed, with many tables, benches, and other items inside damaged. Fortunately, no one was inside at the time, so no accidents occurred. However, according to nearby residents, when the lightning struck, the sound was so loud that it was several times louder than the firing of a cannon, causing those who heard it to be frightened. They only saw golden serpents dancing in the air, and the smell of sulfur and smoke filled their noses. After the rain, they learned that the Yang Wang Temple had been struck by lightning. However, an inspection of the collapsed area revealed no special phenomena. Only a huge courtyard pillar inside the building was struck in half by the lightning.

Seventy-Two Dozen Wood Thread Balls Recovered 154

Hua Cheng Factory Takes Back First

Wang Zhizhuang Sentenced to Imprisonment and Fine

The Hua Cheng Wood Thread Ball Factory on Kaifeng Road had previously been defrauded of 360 dozen thread balls. Subsequently, Xu A'mei, a woman from Wusong, was arrested for selling the stolen goods on behalf of the factory. Then, the swindler Wang Zhizhuang was arrested on Avenue Edward VII. Both were sent to the Special District Local Court for interrogation and detention, as detailed in previous reports. The stolen thread balls have now been recovered by the factory, led by a detective, from the Zhong Xing Clothing Store at No. 48 Hubei Road, the Cheng Chang Pawnshop at No. 54 Avenue Dubail, the Hong Chang Pawnshop at No. 44 Avenue Magill, No. 10 Avenue Kirock, and No. 24 Ximen Bizhou Road, totaling 72 dozen. In addition, some were also found, so only 40 dozen are missing. The court held another hearing the day before yesterday. Zhu Sifei, a lawyer representing the Hua Cheng Factory, appeared in court and stated that Wang Zhizhuang had used the alias Wang Daming when defrauding the factory. He requested punishment and filed a private prosecution to recover the value of the goods. Judge Xu verified the statements and immediately sentenced Wang Zhizhuang to three years in prison and a fine of 300 yuan. Xu A'mei was sentenced to six months in prison and a fine of 100 yuan. If the fine cannot be paid, it can be commuted to one day of imprisonment for every two yuan. The counterfeit stamps were confiscated. Wang Zhizhuang must also compensate the plaintiff for the goods worth 71 yuan, and the stolen goods were returned to the plaintiff.

Machine Purchase Scam Unsuccessful 155

Fake Zhuang Tickets Did Not Match

The Nanfang Heji Machine Company, located at the northern end of Xiaoximen on Zhonghua Road in this city, has been open for more than ten years and is known for manufacturing sock machines. Recently, due to increased investment and expansion, it reopened the day before yesterday. Many people ordered machines at once. Just as they were busy receiving customers, a man dressed in Western clothes, wearing leather shoes and glasses, around thirty years old, claiming to be Jiang Hongxiang, a purchasing agent for the Jiangyin Chengxin Weaving Company,

Page 16

came to the company to order five sock machines, five machines for woolen shirts, scarves and gloves, and hardware parts, stating that he needed the goods immediately. The company's manager, Lu Jinfan, and assistant manager, Zhou Zhusheng, said that most of the sock machines had already been ordered by other factories. Because Jiang was eager to ship them to Jiangyin, they agreed to give Jiang's purchase priority, agreeing on a price of 867.5 taels of silver. They instructed Jiang to send the goods to No. 6 Xinjiangli, western section of Avenue Lafayette that day and pay cash. The company's manager immediately supervised the workers to pack the machines and send them to the address on a flatbed cart. Jiang took the goods and gave a fake Zhuang ticket from Yuanda near the ball field, worth 1,000 taels of silver, instructing the manager to return more than 130 taels of silver. Lu, fearing that the Zhuang ticket was not real, immediately took the ticket and went to check it out. However, he searched the vicinity of the ball field and found no Yuanda Bank. Jiang waited for him to check the ticket, then instructed the freight clerk to go back, but the freight clerk refused. Jiang, knowing that his plan would not work, immediately fled without a trace. When Lu found that the ticket was invalid and returned to the address, he searched for the swindler in vain. He inquired with the second landlord, an old woman surnamed Lu, who said that the swindler had come three days ago to rent the downstairs room, saying that he wanted to set up a wholesale store for woolen socks, etc., agreeing to a monthly rent of 18 yuan, with a writing desk and a tea table renting for 1.2 yuan per month, paying a deposit of 5 yuan and agreeing to move in the next day. The door had a sign that said "Jiangchengxin Weaving Company Shenzhuang." At this point, Manager Lu knew that he had encountered a scammer, and it was fortunate that the goods had not been swindled away. He ordered the staff to return the goods to the company and, fearing that other businesses would be victims of the same scam, he telephoned other businesses to warn them to be careful.

Sanshin Yarn Factory Carelessness 156

Wood and Coffins Reduced to Ashes

The Sanshin Yarn Factory's lumber room at No. 87 Yangshupu Road suddenly caught fire at around 5:10 yesterday morning. Because the stored materials were mostly flammable wood, the fire quickly burned fiercely. The Yangshupu Fire Brigade, upon receiving the news, immediately drove to the scene to extinguish the fire, which was extinguished after about an hour and a half. The loss was about 2,000 yuan. It is said that the cause of the fire was that the gatekeeper was cooking snacks, and sparks flew into the wood shavings, causing them to burn. Most of the items made in the lumber room were coffins, which the factory used to give away as acts of charity.

Zhang Shijin Loses Both Wife and Money

Zhang Shijin, a 36-year-old from Gaoyou, lives at No. 575 Haichang Road, Zhabei. He works as a porter with a very small monthly income, so Zhang is nearly forty years old and still unmarried. A few days ago, a friend from Xinghua, Yu Hanqing, mentioned that Ren Younian's sister-in-law, Zhang Qiaozi, who is 25 years old, is quite beautiful. Because her family is poor, she is eager to find someone to marry and spend her life with. If interested, he can make an introduction at a small cost. Although the relationship between the two was harmonious after Qiaozi entered the house, she suddenly changed her mind in less than half a month. All of his sister-in-law, Zhang Qiaozi, had previously been married to a son of the Pan family in the countryside. However, because her husband's family was poor and unable to make a living, she had to escape and stay at his house. But he made a living pulling rickshaws and could not provide for her, so last month, his friend Yu Hanqing introduced her to Zhang Shijin. This time, she suddenly escaped again, which he knew nothing about. The station chief, seeing that the case was inconsistent and might involve collusion, ordered him to prepare a document and transfer it to the Shanghai Local Court for interrogation.

Inner Tongsha Lightship Temporarily Removed 170

Notice from Xi, patrol engineer of the Maritime Affairs Section of the Customs Administration of the Republic of China: This patrol engineer has investigated and found that the Jiuduan (commonly known as Inner Tongsha) lightship at the entrance to the Yangtze River channel within the jurisdiction of the Jianghai Customs Service is being temporarily removed and replaced with another lightship. The situation and dimensions are listed below. The Jiuduan lightship at the entrance to the Yangtze River channel will be temporarily removed on or about October 7 of this year and replaced with another lightship. No further notice will be given at that time. The replacement lightship is painted with red sides and has no name. It is equipped with a fourth-order white lens light that flashes for one second and is extinguished for five seconds every ten seconds. In clear weather, it can be seen from eleven nautical miles. In the event of cloudy weather or heavy fog, a warning fog bell will be struck once every fifteen seconds. From sunset to sunrise, a white light is hung twelve feet above the bow of the ship to indicate the direction of the bow. Once the repairs to the Jiuduan lightship are completed, it will be reinstalled in its original location, and the replacement lightship will be removed. No further notice will be given at that time. The Hydrographic Chart No. 1 issued by the Maritime Affairs Bureau should be corrected accordingly. Therefore, all ships are hereby notified to pay close attention and remember the details to avoid any omissions. Do not forget! This notice is issued on September 4th of the 19th year of the Republic of China.

The question was how to handle this matter. It was resolved: 1. to send a letter to the company to protest; 2. to send a letter to the General Labor Union of the head office to unanimously reject the transfer. (4) The Standing Committee proposed that Li Zhonggong, the new general manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, would soon take office, and the union should consider how to respond. It was resolved that the Standing Committee members would visit him and inquire about the fundamental measures for the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company.

The Federation of Electricity and Water Industries Unions held its sixth regular meeting yesterday, chaired by Hu Peiji. Matters discussed: (1) The Standing Committee proposed that Comrade Xu had sent a letter firmly resigning from the position of director of the registration section of the union. The question was whether to approve this. It was resolved to approve. (2) The Standing Committee proposed that a request had previously been submitted to the municipal authorities to appoint Zhang Pinzhang as a preparatory committee member of the union, but the appointment had not yet been seen. It was proposed to urge the municipal authorities to expedite the appointment to facilitate work. It was resolved to submit the request. (3) [Omitted]. (4) Zhu Hanhe proposed that the union should find ways to organize labor unions for all electrical workers in Zhenru, Wusong, Yinxiang Port, and other places, as they were within the city limits, but the number of workers was unknown. It was proposed to nominate people to investigate the number of workers in each place. It was resolved to nominate Yang Chunfang and Ding Song’an to be responsible for the investigation. [Omitted].

The Preparatory Committee of the Cotton Mill Workers’ Federation held its fifth meeting yesterday, chaired by Li Changgen. After conducting the ritual, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting (omitted). Matters discussed: (1) The Standing Committee proposed that a notice should be issued to all factory unions to register with the federation as soon as possible to facilitate the progress of work. It was resolved that the registration section would handle this in conjunction with the guidance section. (2) The Standing Committee proposed that the workers in the various factories in the industry were of mixed quality, and there was concern that they would be exploited by the Communists. The union planned to issue a declaration warning workers not to be used by the Communists. The question was whether this was appropriate. It was resolved that the document department would handle this. They requested that officials be sent to reorganize the union’s affairs to maintain the labor movement. It was resolved: A. to issue an order to the union to cease activities and await the dispatch of personnel for reorganization; B. to submit a report to the Municipal People's Training Committee for record. (4) The Standing Committee proposed that the union affairs of the Xihe Cotton Mill were at a standstill and that the Municipal People’s Training Committee should be requested to send personnel to reorganize the union to maintain the labor movement. The question was whether this was appropriate. It was resolved to approve. (5) The guidance section proposed that the workers of the Ri Hua Cotton Mill in Pudong were demanding a daily rice subsidy of one dime from the capitalists, but the capitalists refused to agree and instead used various means to oppress the workers. The workers had no choice but to strike for seven weeks, but the matter was still not resolved satisfactorily. If this continued, the workers would be left to die. The union should request the Municipal People’s Training Committee to immediately convene all industry unions in the city to organize a support committee to provide assistance. The question was whether this was appropriate. It was resolved to approve. The meeting was adjourned.

Submission

Declaration of the Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi Anti-Communist and People's Salvation Association 173

The crimes of the Communists were exposed during the Wuhan government era. Although the Kuomintang's anti-communism led to some restraint, the seeds of disaster spread throughout the country. Zhu and Mao led armed Red Armies that roamed the provinces of Jiangxi, Fujian, and Guangdong for three years without being wiped out. Knowledgeable people knew early on that this spark would be enough to set the plains ablaze. In the past year, the disaster caused by the Communists has intensified, causing countless people across the country to lose their homes and lives, especially the people of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces. In Jiangxi province, over three-quarters of the province's eighty-odd counties have been ravaged by the Communists. Those who survive and live in terror are only along the Nanchang to Jiujiang line. In Hubei province, over two-thirds of the province's sixty-odd counties have been ravaged by the Communists, forming a major encirclement of the three towns of Wuhan. People who previously considered Wuhan a refuge are now in a state of panic, not knowing when their lives will end. In Hunan province, western Hunan has long become a Communist stronghold, and eastern Hunan has been repeatedly massacred by the Communists. Changsha, a major city in the province, has recently been reported to have fallen. Schools were destroyed, consulates were destroyed, shops were destroyed, residences were destroyed, and government offices were destroyed. In a matter of days, the entire city was almost reduced to a wasteland. Famous teachers and respected scholars were all killed as being senile and ignorant. Well-to-do families were all killed as being landlords and local bullies. Clerks were all killed as being corrupt officials. Scholars were all killed as being intellectuals. Those who were lucky enough to escape were in imminent danger, unable to support themselves. This is a tragic event unprecedented in history, and all patriots and people of goodwill who hear of it cannot help but feel heartbroken. Moreover, the disaster caused by the Communists is not limited to Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces. In Guangdong, southern Fujian, northern Jiangsu, eastern Sichuan, and northern Anhui, the disaster is not as severe as in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces, but it has been brewing for a long time, and the signs of disaster are already visible. If not addressed urgently, these areas may become the next Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces. The reason why the Communists are rampant in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces is that they want to take advantage of the turmoil in the Central Plains, to connect the Communists of the three provinces to form a central force, and then to establish contact with the Communists of nearby provinces to communize the entire country and submit to Soviet Russia. Therefore, the safety of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi provinces is not only related to the survival of the people of the three provinces, but can also predetermine the fate of the people of the entire country. The people of our three provinces must unite and thoroughly oppose communism to save themselves from the current crisis. The people of other provinces must not stand idly by and do nothing. If they think that the disaster has not yet reached them and remain indifferent, and then run away when the disaster strikes, China is so large that there may be nowhere to escape. If those with ambition can rise up righteously to save the people who are suffering from communism and take on the responsibility of eradicating the Communists, and if everyone can work together with one heart, we can certainly wipe out the Communists and reverse the catastrophe of the country. By saving others, we can also save ourselves. Is this not better than sitting and waiting for death? The members of this association, seeing this situation, have formed this association in the hope of encouraging each other. The aims we advocate are stated in the charter. We only know how to oppose communism and save the people, and we do not ask about anything else. Anyone who shares our sentiments is welcome to provide assistance. Those who wish to become members and fight together are especially welcome. This declaration is hereby made.

The Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi Anti-Communist and People's Salvation Association Charter: Article 1: The sole purpose of this association is to eradicate the Communists and save the people. It will absolutely not involve military, political, or partisan issues. Article 2: Anyone who supports the purpose of this association, pays the membership fee and annual fee stipulated by this association, and is introduced by one or more members of this association may become a member of this association. Article 3: Members of this association, regardless of their province of origin, are divided into two types: 1. Ordinary members: an entrance fee of five yuan and an annual fee of two yuan, but farmers, workers, shop assistants, and young students only pay an entrance fee of fifty cents and an annual fee of twenty cents; 2. Special members: anyone who especially supports this association may join this association as a special member, with an entrance fee of fifty yuan and an annual fee of ten yuan. Article 4: In addition to fulfilling the obligations in the previous article, members of this association are especially welcome to promote the purpose of this association, introduce members, solicit donations, and secretly inquire about information about the bandits. Article 5: Members of this association who wish to take on the work of this association are free to choose to do so. This association will often provide strategies to facilitate progress. Article 6: The main affairs of this association are as follows: 1. to investigate the actual situation of the Communists in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi and the actual situation of the disasters caused by communism; 2. to provide relief to the people of Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi who have suffered from communism; 3. to publish publications to announce the crimes of the Communists in order to awaken the people's attention and enable them to effectively oppose communism in advance; 4. to study various specific anti-communist methods in politics, military affairs, education, and society for use by all parties; 5. to expose the Communists who are hidden in various places, groups, and organizations, as well as books and newspapers with red tints, in order to awaken all parties to directly punish them; 6. to contact and support all forces that are actually opposing communism; 7. to assist the people in organizing communist eradication groups to eliminate the Communists themselves, in order to assist the local authorities. Article 7: This association will establish a general headquarters in Hankou, and branch associations in Changsha and Jiujiang. In various counties and other provinces, this association may hire several people as propagandists. Article 8: The general headquarters and branch associations of this association will each have one president and several vice presidents, who will be publicly elected by this association from among enthusiastic anti-communist and people-saving individuals. Article 9: The general headquarters and branch associations of this association will each establish a secretariat under the president to carry out all the affairs of this association. Article 10: The secretariat will have one secretary-general to manage the affairs, and several secretaries to manage the affairs separately. Article 11: The secretariat will temporarily establish the following four sections. If deemed necessary, it may be increased. The tasks of each section are as follows: 1. General Affairs Section: specifically manages documents, registration, and accounting matters; 2. Investigation Section: specifically manages the investigation of communist disasters and the reporting of communist matters; 3. Propaganda Section: specifically manages editing and research matters; 4. Relief Section: specifically manages refugee relief matters. Article 12: The secretary-general and secretaries of the general headquarters will be publicly elected by the initiators. After one year, they will be publicly elected annually by all members. Article 13: The secretary-general and secretaries of the branch associations will be appointed by the general headquarters. Article 14: This association may solicit donations from enthusiastic people outside the association in the name of this association. Article 15: This association has the following obligations to its members: 1. If a member suffers from disaster due to anti-communism after joining the association, this association must provide relief as a priority; 2. If a member fears being resented by the Communists and does not wish to disclose their name, this association shall keep it confidential or announce it under a pseudonym; 3. Members may read the periodic publications issued by this association without compensation; 4. A report on the association's affairs will be published and distributed to members every year; 5. To answer members' inquiries about anti-communist methods. Article 16: If a member violates the purpose of this association or hinders the progress of this association, they may be immediately declared expelled. Article 17: This association shall be declared dissolved when the Communists in Hunan, Hubei, and Jiangxi are eliminated.

Oriental Daily's View of Sino-Foreign Trade 175

A National Harvest Means Fundamental Trade Conditions are in Place; Hope for an Early End to Internal Warfare to Promote Economic Activity

An Osaka Asahi Shimbun editorial states: China's foreign trade typically reaches its peak in the second half of the year. As China is an agricultural nation, its purchasing power depends on the abundance or scarcity of agricultural products. According to reports from Chinese sources, the planting this year has benefited from suitable weather throughout the country, with sunshine and rain in good balance, resulting in a rare harvest in recent years. In the three northeastern provinces, which are rich in agricultural products, the planting has been excellent, and security is assured, which is a great difference from last year when the Russian-Chinese conflict caused disturbances.

Furthermore, according to news from Shandong, the planting in the provinces of Shandong, Hebei, and Henan this year has been an unusually bountiful harvest. Sorghum, millet, peanuts, tobacco, and other crops are expected to increase in yield, some even doubling the normal yield. Wheat planting in the spring was also quite good. This shows that North China, which has been suffering from a major drought for the past two or three years, has gradually escaped its plight, and this is also evidence of the easing of the severe drought in Shaanxi and Gansu. This summer, Henan province has also experienced frequent rainfall, which has been absent for the past two or three years. Henan's harvest can also cultivate the purchasing power of farmers and stimulate foreign trade. This is not limited to Henan.

The provinces south of the Yangtze River are different from North China, often suffering from poor harvests due to excessive rainfall. This year, there have been no reports of areas suffering from floods. It is feared that this year's harvest will be a general harvest across the country, which has already laid the fundamental conditions for stimulating foreign trade to reach its peak in the second half of the year. However, in order to fully realize these conditions, there is a prerequisite that must be fulfilled. This is none other than the hope that the internal warfare that straddles the three provinces of Henan, Shandong, and Hebei will end quickly. If the war ends soon, agricultural products can be freely transported, and there is hope for peace in the future. Then, the economic activities that have been suppressed by war and famine will suddenly be promoted, and the trade in the second half of this year will see unexpected prosperity.

Looking at the trade situation in July of this year, it already shows vitality. Among them, the business situation in Guangdong is particularly prosperous, and it also stimulates the Shanghai market. This is because although Guangdong suffered from the challenge of the Gui faction in the first half of this year, with continuous warfare, and the Gui faction entered Hunan in May and June, the two Guang provinces have returned to stability. Once the continuous warfare ends, the economic world there will immediately be revived, as we have seen.

Therefore, the results of Sino-Foreign trade in the second half of this year depend on how quickly the war is quelled. Today, Shanghai's silver reserves are 220 million taels, which is a special reason for the sharp drop in silver prices. If, during this year's national bumper harvest, internal turmoil is quelled and temporary peace is achieved, Shanghai's silver capital will be absorbed by the inland rural areas, and the sharp drop in silver prices will be greatly eased. Moreover, the rampage of the Communist bandits who disturb the Jiangnan area is caused by the lack of security due to internal warfare. Considering the great impact of this on trade, we cannot help but hope for a swift end to the war.

Chinese Cocoons Imported to Japan Transform into Japanese Cocoons Imported to China 176

About 200 piculs of Japanese Cocoons to be Experimentally Imported

According to the Oriental Daily News, the Shanghai-based Japanese commercial attaché Yokotake telegraphed on the 28th that Chinese customs recently levied a 12.5% ad valorem import tax on Japanese cocoons that were being experimentally imported. At the request of the Jiangsu-Zhejiang Silk Industry Association, the National Government plans to reduce the ad valorem tax to 7.5% for a total of 60,000 piculs over six months starting in October and will notify customs accordingly. According to industry sources, only about 200 piculs of Japanese cocoons are being experimentally imported. With the current Japanese market price, a tax of 12.5% is not very cost-effective. However, with a tax of 7.5%, converted at the original price, about 690 taels, a considerable import is expected. However, although a good autumn silkworm harvest is generally expected this year, it is still doubtful how much demand will be stimulated. In short, the fact that only Chinese cocoons have been imported to Japan in the past, but now Japanese cocoons are being imported to China, is worth noting.

Japanese Ministry of Agriculture Takes Charge of Fishery Negotiations 178

Officials to Be Stationed in the Russian Capital and Khabarovsk

Tokyo News: Due to the increasingly frequent fishery negotiations between Japan and Russia, the Japanese Ministry of Agriculture and Forestry believes that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs is not familiar with the fishery situation and that it is inconvenient to negotiate on its behalf. At the request of the fishery industry, the ministry plans to establish one higher-level official and one subordinate official in Khabarovsk and Moscow, totaling four people, to handle fishery negotiations. The ministry has included 80,000 yuan in its budget for the coming year to realize this plan.

Mr. Ding Monong's Recent Work 180

Brave Young Woman 181

— Jùn Shān

The American youth seem to indulge in pleasure and dislike work much more than our own youth. However, their youth community does not lack outstanding, brave, self-sacrificing, and self-respecting individuals, who can shoulder the responsibility of revitalizing the nation. Such young people are truly admirable and the real masters of the country. The young woman introduced here is also a leader in this regard.

Miss Lenore Cook graduated from the University of Wisconsin a few years ago. She is about to embark on a three-year round-the-world voyage with four men in a 40-foot yawl. One of the four men is Lenore's husband, a graduate of Northwestern University's School of Journalism and a renowned amateur photographer. Lenore's duties on the ship are as cook and doctor.

According to their planned route, their sailboat, named "Swordfish," will depart from Chicago in the near future, heading to Bermuda, then through the Panama Canal. From there, they will cross the Pacific Ocean, sailing thousands of nautical miles to New Zealand and Australia, then north through the Malay Archipelago, through the Suez Canal, to Greece and Italy, through the Strait of Gibraltar, to the coasts of Spain and France. They will then circumnavigate the continent, cross the Atlantic Ocean to the east coast of America, up the St. Lawrence River, to the Great Lakes. They plan to return to Chicago in 1933 for the exhibition.

Besides the Cooks, the other three are also worth mentioning. The captain, Orr Evans, is a Harvard University football star. Paul, his brother, is also a member of the Yale football team and will serve as the ship's engineer. Donold Dickinson, 21, is a graduate of St. John's Military Academy and will be the ship's radio operator.

The Cooks plan to document everything about their trip.

Guidelines for Social News Submissions 182

(1) Articles should be limited to news about domestic and international science, industry, commerce, rural sanitation, aviation, exploration, customs, or urban life.

(2) Illustrations should be limited to various lyrical paintings related to social life.

(3) Photographs should be qualified by capturing the seasons, landscapes, flora and fauna, people, and news events. Photographs of beautiful women in seasonal landscapes are especially welcome.

(4) The number of words per article should not exceed 2,000.

(5) Do not write on both sides of the manuscript paper.

(6) Do not write manuscripts horizontally. Write legibly. Western text should be minimized; if it must be quoted, include the original text below the translation.

(8) Do not use blue ink for illustrations, and do not use colored paper. Use white paper and black ink.

(8) Please address submissions to the "Social News Editorial Department."

(9) Submissions will not be returned regardless of whether they are published, unless a request for return is made in advance.

(10) Compensation for text is divided into three levels: three yuan, two yuan, or one yuan per thousand words. Compensation for illustrations and photographs follows the same rates per item. Special contributions will be compensated separately.
